Small Steamer Sinks After Collision 145

Two Foremen Tragically Drown; Customs Detains Xin Shuntai

The Linxing, a small steamer owned by the Songhu Maoxing Company, was sailing to the Yawosha sea off the Sancha Estuary of Wusong at 10:30 PM the day before yesterday (14th) to tow a timber boat from Fujian to Shanghai. At the same time, another small steamer, Xin Shuntai, also arrived. The two small steamers, competing for business, both accelerated and rushed to arrive first. When they were about to reach the timber boat, the Linxing was accidentally collided with by the Xin Shuntai. At the same time, the sea breeze was strong, and the Linxing immediately sank. Huang Helou, a 30-year-old foreman from Yiqiao, Zhejiang, drowned because he could not escape. His body has not yet been recovered. The other four sailors were fortunate enough to climb onto the timber boat and were rescued. After Zhang Huabang Customs learned of the incident, they boarded a customs small steamer and rushed to the scene of the accident to inspect it for a week. They then took the Xin Shuntai, which caused the accident, to Zhang Huabang and detained it. Meanwhile, Maoxing Company filed a report with the customs to negotiate with Xin Shuntai for compensation.

French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association Protests the Dong Wenli Case; Yesterday, a Letter Was Sent to the French Consul General for Investigation and Handling 146

The French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association, regarding the case of merchant Dong Wenli being illegally searched by the French police and falsely accused of opening a gambling establishment, jointly petitioned the French Concession authorities the day before yesterday, but it has not been resolved for a month. At the same time, the Jiangtui Association in Shanghai also sent a letter to the association making the same request. The association sent a letter to the French Consul General (Badas) yesterday to negotiate on reasonable grounds. A reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency has recorded the original text below:

"Respectfully, according to a letter from various merchants with their seals, on the night of February 12 this year at 8:00 PM, a large number of French police officers went to Wang Shunxing Wood Shop at 206 Avenue Foch, claiming to be searching for gambling, and violently beat apprentices and arrested merchants, framing Dong Wenli. More than two weeks have passed, and there is still no solution. The public is panicked and restless. At the time of the incident, the merchants were outraged by what they heard and saw. They all believed that the police's search of shops was often based on rumors and anonymous letters. This kind of reckless action is enough to make residents unable to sleep peacefully. Since the case has been found to be unfounded, four merchants and one ignorant apprentice who were playing mahjong were arrested. Afterwards, they tried to frame Dong Wenli and monitor his actions. It was later heard that various groups came forward to negotiate, but there was no response. Their attempts to cover up their mistakes are even more obvious. Our stores are deeply chilled when we think of this. Therefore, we jointly affix our seals and petition your association to lodge a serious protest and send a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the French authorities seriously. At the same time, we ask the court that the concession police should apply to the court for a search warrant before searching residents in the future to show caution and avoid abuses, etc. We are currently reviewing the matter. The Jianghuai Association in Shanghai also sent a letter saying that the French police's illegal search and framing of our association member Dong Wenli was caused by the police inspector Qian Chenglong abusing his power and arbitrarily fabricating the case. Now that the truth has been clarified, we request that your association send a letter to the French authorities to investigate and handle the matter strictly to deter others and reassure the residents. Based on this, we respectfully report the case and ask you to investigate and handle it and reply to us so that we can inform you. Sincerely, the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association, to Mr. Badas, French Consul General in Shanghai."

Quarrel Over Changing Dishes Leads to Restaurant Waiter's Sudden Death; Autopsy Reveals Relapse of Heart Disease 147

At 8:00 PM the night before last (15th), Gao Huaibao, a barber shop owner from Yangzhou, invited guests to Qingpingyuan Restaurant at No. 7, the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and West Xinqiao Street in the French Concession. He invited his fellow townsman Wang Jilong (37 years old), who lived at No. 62 Lagenal Road in the French Concession, to be the host. Halfway through the meal, Wang ordered the waiter Meng Xiangqing (31 years old, from Yangzhou, living at No. 64, Fengyuli, Saposai Road) to change two dishes according to the menu. Meng refused to change them. When Wang settled the bill at the end of the meal, Wang blamed Meng for refusing to change the dishes. The two then quarreled and were persuaded to stop. Wang went home immediately, and Meng went to work on the third floor. Unexpectedly, after the quarrel, he was overwhelmed with anger, his face turned pale gray, and he could not stand still and fell down. He immediately hired a car to send Meng to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital across the street from the Dashijie on Xizang Road for treatment. Unexpectedly, he died when he arrived at the hospital. His family reported to the French police, saying that he had died of anger after quarreling with the customer Wang Jilong and requested an investigation. The police officer approved the request and sent a detective to send the body to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall. One side brought Wang to the case. Yesterday, the police station summoned the deceased's mother, Meng Wangshi, and the witnesses Zhang Rongxi, the owner of Qingpingyuan, and Guo Honglin, another waiter, to the case. They reported to the Second Special Court Procuratorate and appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren to come to the office with the forensic doctor, the clerk, etc., at noon to examine the body. The autopsy revealed that the deceased died of a relapse of old heart disease and that there was no other cause. After the autopsy, they took their seats in the court. First, West Detective Henry and Chinese Detective Zhang Chunsheng reported the investigation process. According to the deposition of the deceased's mother, Meng Wangshi, she said that the deceased was her son and had suffered from stomach problems before his death. Last night, he died of anger after a quarrel. The defendant Wang Jilong confessed that he had a slight quarrel with the deceased over changing dishes, but it was not fierce. The two were quickly persuaded to stop. According to the statements of the witnesses Zhang Rongxi, Guo Honglin, and the deceased's old man, Huang Huanwen, the official ruled that Meng Xiangqing died of illness during his lifetime, and the body was handed over to the deceased's relative, Meng Wangshi, for burial. Whether the defendant Wang Jilong was at fault will be investigated and handled by the police department.

Woman's Death from Quitting Opium 148

Autopsy Reveals Death from Illness While Quitting Opium

Xie Xu, a 37-year-old woman from Pudong, lived with her husband, Xie Linkui (a tailor), at No. 307 Tongfu Road. She was physically weak and addicted to opium for seven or eight years. Recently, she suddenly felt that this was inconvenient and became disgusted with it. She then repeatedly asked someone to help her quit this addiction. On the 12th of this month, through the introduction of someone, she found Xu Yongshi (34 years old, from Tongzhou), a quack doctor living at No. 88 Robison Road, to help her quit. At that time, it was agreed that it would cost 45 yuan, and 20 yuan would be paid first. Then, Xu bought the medicine and ordered her to decoct and take it, stipulating that she should eat it every six hours, for a total of six times. After taking it, she would be able to quit. Unexpectedly, her illness suddenly became serious after taking the medicine for the fifth time, and she died before the day before yesterday. Her husband believed that his wife's death was caused by Xu, so he called Xu to his house and argued with him, saying that he would not settle the matter unless he paid 2,000 yuan. Then they quarreled and wrestled with each other to the Chengdu Road police station. After the police officer inquired about the situation, he ordered Detective Xie Guisheng and others to investigate. He then sent the body to the autopsy room on Pei Tou Road. Yesterday morning, Song Genshan, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Local Court, and forensic doctors Wei and Zhang, the clerk, etc., came to the office to examine the body. Xie Linkui said that he was 43 years old and that the deceased was his wife. Recently, she wanted to quit smoking. Through the introduction of someone, she asked Xu to come, but after eating his medicine, she became ill and died. Therefore, he asked for justice. Xu Yongshi said that his opium-quitting medicine was a family secret recipe. He had given it to seven or eight people to decoct and take, and the results were good. He bought the medicine for her, which contained the medicine "wind eggplant flower," which would temporarily make people dizzy after eating, but it was not life-threatening. Judge Song then told the husband of the deceased that, according to the forensic doctor of our court, the cause of your wife's death was still illness. If you still have any doubts, our court can dissect the body for examination. However, he was unwilling. Judge Song then ruled that the deceased Xie Xu was a woman who died of illness while quitting opium. The body was handed over to her husband, Xie Linkui, for burial after he signed a statement.

However, at that time, everyone was panicked and only saw Gu fall to the ground motionless, so they did not have time to check whether he was dead before scattering and fleeing. Yao Jinping, Who Transformed from Female to Male, Has Arrived in Shanghai 150

Her Vivid Account is Like a Fantasy; Witnesses and Evidence Suggest it is True; Worthy of Study by Physiologists

Datong News Agency reports: It was reported by Shenshi News Agency's Tianjin telegram on the 15th that Yao Youtang's daughter, an officer of Li Du's troops, suddenly underwent physiological changes upon hearing thunder and transformed into a male body. It was also said that the person had already left Beijing and come to Shanghai. The suddenness of the matter made it hard to believe as true. However, yesterday morning, a Datong News Agency reporter learned from General Li Du that this matter was indeed true and that the person had already arrived in Shanghai. After many turns, the reporter was able to meet the person and obtained two photos related to the matter, which made him believe that the world is full of wonders. The reporter records the situation below for the study of physiologists.

A Brief Account of Yao Jinping, Who Transformed from Female to Male

Yesterday morning, a Datong News Agency reporter visited General Li Du and confirmed that the news was true. The reporter then went to her residence in the French Concession and met the protagonist of this female-to-male transformation, Yao Jinping (not Jinbing), who is from Zhongjie, Qingxian County, Hebei. She is 20 years old this year. Her father, Yao Huating (Youtang is his alias), studied at the Baoding Military Academy. During Zhang Zongchang's rule in Shandong, he served as a staff officer in Yao Yunke's Eighth Division. Later, he went to Jilin to serve as the captain of the police academy. After the September 18th Incident, he joined Li Du's Volunteer Army and served as the chief of staff of the First Division of the Jilin Self-Defense Army.

Transformation upon Hearing Thunder

Because of the defeat in the war of resistance, he retreated with the army into Russian territory. After detouring to Xinjiang, there was no news of him, and his fate was unknown. Therefore, Jinping, at her home, missed her father so much that she cried day and night. The transformation from female to male also occurred in this way. According to Yao Qingpu (Yao Jinping's grandfather, who accompanied Jinping to Shanghai this time), on the evening of the 21st day of the seventh lunar month of last year, Jinping was lying on her bed in the small building, thinking sadly of her father, when she heard a loud thunder. The roof tiles of the small building shook. At that time, Jinping immediately felt something. The next day, she shyly told her mother, Mrs. Zhang, that she had transformed into a man. Her mother thought it was a joke and tried to feel through her trousers, and indeed felt something extra.

Inspecting the Dignified Man

At that time, the whole family was extremely surprised. According to the woman, in a dream that night, an old woman said to her, "You have transformed into a male body. From now on, you can look for your father and fulfill your wish. However, you must wait a hundred days before you can show your lower body to others, otherwise it will not be auspicious." After a full hundred days, the family took off her pants and examined her, and indeed, she was a dignified man. The above is all from the talk of her grandfather Yao Qingpu. Given his old age and simplicity, he would not deceive us. However, the matter is indeed somewhat akin to a fantasy.

Documents Proving the Facts

Yesterday morning, the reporter personally saw Yao Jinping. Although she was no different from an ordinary man, she was quite shy when meeting people. She seemed to have bound her feet as a child, so she still showed signs of bent feet. The pierced earring holes had not disappeared. This is where she differs from ordinary men. Her grandfather Yao Qingpu also showed the reporter one photo of her before the transformation and one after the transformation, which seemed to prove that the matter was not false. At the same time, there was also a diploma from the girls' school she attended in her hometown in 1929, which is recorded below. Her grandfather Yao Qingpu also said that before leaving Tianjin, they stayed at the Qi family in Dongjia Hutong, Xiaoguan, Hebei. When they talked about this matter, the neighbors were in an uproar. The police also sent officers to investigate, which was very troublesome. Therefore, he asked the reporter not to announce the location of their Shanghai residence.

Joining the Army to Find Her Father, Li Persuaded Her Not To

Since transforming into a male body, Yao Jinping has changed her name to Yao Zhen and her style name to Gengsheng. She arrived in Shanghai on the 8th of this month and visited General Li Du and his wife. Regarding joining the army to find her father, Li advised her not to because she was young and her parents were old. The reporter now records her girls' school graduation diploma below: "Certificate of Completion: Student Yao Jinping is from Qingxian County, Hebei Province, is 15 years old this year, and has completed the four-year course at this school. Her examination results are passing. This certifies. Yao Zhengqian, Principal of the Qingxian Public Zhongjie Girls' Elementary School, July 2nd, Republic of China 19."

New Vehicles Arrive in Shanghai 153

Special Longhua Buses Added Starting Yesterday

Route 4 Will be Implemented After the Incense Season; Route 5's Road Surface is Being Paved by the Public Works Bureau

The Shanghai Nanpu Public Bus Management Office of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau has ordered new-style Da Meng Tian vehicles from the United States. It has begun operating special Longhua incense season buses starting yesterday. The details are recorded below.

New Vehicles Arrive in Shanghai

The Shanghai Nanpu Public Bus Management Office has ordered a total of twelve new-style public buses from the American Da Meng Tian Automobile Manufacturing Company. Each vehicle costs more than 10,000 yuan. The vehicle body is made of pure zinc-copper. Two vehicles have already arrived in Shanghai, and the remaining ten vehicles will arrive within a day or two. The new vehicles are similar to the public buses in the concession. Passengers enter and exit through the side doors. The seats are divided into front and rear sections. All equipment inside the vehicle is new and beautiful.

Special Buses Added

Every spring, Longhua has an incense season near Qingming Festival. The number of tourists is double that of previous years. Usually, there are only six public buses running in both directions. Now that the incense season has arrived, the existing vehicles are not enough to meet demand. Now that the new vehicles have arrived in Shanghai, the office has started operating special Longhua incense season buses starting yesterday. The fare remains the same and has not increased.

Route 4

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, in order to develop traffic in southern Shanghai, plans to open new routes 4 and 5. The stations and fares for Route 4 have been determined, with Dapu Bridge as the terminus. After the incense season, all the new vehicles will be used on this route. As for the cross-city route 5, the road surface is uneven and is being paved by the Public Works Bureau. Therefore, the official implementation date has not yet been determined.

Visitors all expressed satisfaction and praise for the exquisite facilities of the pier and the floating restaurant. Until 5:00 PM in the afternoon, those who came to visit were still streaming in.

Pier Facilities

The pier is made entirely of steel plates and is divided into upper and lower layers. The lower layer has waiting areas for passengers taking long-distance and cross-river ferries, reading areas, and tea rooms, and is also equipped with a Xiang Sheng taxi rental office and public telephones. The upper layer's northern end is the business department office, first-class ticket office, and the Trust Society's Bund office. The middle part is the first-class passenger waiting area, and the southern part is the floating restaurant. The pier is surrounded by steel windows on both the upper and lower levels. There is water heating in winter and electric fans in summer. All decorations are extremely beautiful and elegant, and cleanliness and order are well maintained.

Floating Restaurant

The floating restaurant on the pier is equipped and decorated with the utmost care. The roof is flat and round, painted with silver-gray paint, and inlaid with silver lines, making it brilliant and dazzling. The electric lights are hidden in the ceiling and walls, as if one is in a city that never sleeps, without any dazzling glare. The steel windows are curtained with ivory-colored gauze curtains, the colors are extremely harmonious, and it is very artistic. The floor is made of teak strips inlaid with patterns, which is exceptionally smooth. Other items, such as spring leather seats and dining tables, are all exquisite, beautiful, and comfortable. The dining hall is large and can accommodate more than a hundred people for meals. There are many rattan tables and chairs on the corridor outside the windows. Customers can enjoy the river view while dining. During this beautiful spring season, it is truly a feeling of pleasure and enjoyment, making people linger. The Western food sold in the restaurant is carefully selected for its ingredients and cooked to taste. In addition, the diesel stoves are cleaner and more hygienic. The various refreshments are also baked by themselves using the latest scientific methods. Especially the coffee, the brewing method is different from others and has a unique flavor. The cleanliness of the waiters' uniforms and their polite demeanor have also been strictly trained. The restaurant will open for business today. It is believed that ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life will rush to enjoy its delicacies.

Requesting the Owner to Extend the Deadline for Relocation

At the intersection of Yinghuali, Laobesheng Road in western Shanghai, there is vacant land of about twenty acres. Because the location is remote and there are few people, most residents from Jiangbei, unable to afford to rent houses, built thatched sheds on the vacant land to live in, totaling about four hundred and sixty rooms, housing more than two thousand four hundred people. Recently, because the landlord Qiasheng Company planned to sell the vacant land, it ordered all the shantytowns to be demolished within two weeks, otherwise, it would be enforced. The shantytowns were unable to relocate at once and demanded that the landlord relocate them at a preferential address, which was not approved. Instead, workers were ordered to build bamboo dams around the land to prevent entry and exit. The shantytowns were panicked. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, they sent representatives Zhu Guangyou, Yue Jisong, Yin Jiafu, Zhao Qike, and dozens of others, carrying petitions to the Municipal Party Department in Fenglin Bridge. Yu Yaoqiu, a staff member of the Investigation Section, received them. The representatives recounted their hardships and requested assistance to avoid displacement. Yu 君 promised to investigate the details first and then 核奪.

Madam Zhou Gu Commits Suicide by Swallowing Raw Opium Due to a Quarrel with Her Husband 161

Madam Zhou Gu, a resident of Suzhou, aged twenty-two, living at No. 1 Yongxiang Lane, Tonglu Road, Zhabei, had a quarrel with her husband yesterday afternoon around 1:00 PM over a trivial matter. Afterwards, feeling aggrieved, she developed a pessimistic outlook on life and secretly swallowed raw opium to commit suicide. Her family discovered her and rushed her to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, due to severe poisoning, the treatment was ineffective, and she died at 7:50 PM. Her body was transferred to the forensic morgue for examination.

Labor Dispute at Changxing Dyeing Factory 163

According to a statement released by the Dyeing Industry Association, Changxing Mercerizing Dyeing Factory, located at No. 17 Ning'an Lane, Weining Road, South Shanghai, was established in the 16th year of the Republic of China by Wu Xinfu as a sole proprietorship. The initial capital was several thousand yuan, and due to business development over the years, the surplus is estimated to be over two hundred thousand yuan. Its success is remarkable and is a rare sight in the dyeing industry. However, the factory suddenly announced its closure in February of this year, claiming poor business performance, which angered all the workers. They reported the matter to the Dyeing Industry Union, which in turn reported it to the Party and government agencies for legal mediation and strictly ordered the employer to resume operations. The case is currently under investigation by the Social Affairs Bureau, but no results have been achieved. To clarify whether the factory's annual business has been profitable or loss-making, the Party and government agencies will entrust an accountant to conduct a legal audit of the accounts and then mediate the matter. In the meantime, the labor side is ordered to await a resolution quietly.

Special Announcement

Jin Cheng Bank 1934 Business Report (4) 173

(2) Non-Gold Standard Countries

The economic situation of non-gold standard countries in recent years includes the so-called gold sterling bloc (represented by the United Kingdom, Canada, Denmark, and Sweden), the U.S. dollar bloc (represented by the United States), and the Japanese yen bloc (represented by Japan). The common policy of these countries is to abandon the gold standard, devalue their currencies through inflation, increase national prices, and increase corporate profits to promote production and reduce unemployment. At the same time, they also encourage exports by lowering foreign exchange rates, which has gradually become effective. The financial, price, production, unemployment, bankruptcy, and trade conditions of these countries are described below.

(1) Finance: Generally speaking, the financial situation is gradually stabilizing and improving and is achieving the expected goals to some extent. Looking at the discount rate of central banks, it has generally been declining since 1932, which proves that the financial situation has become increasingly stable. Looking at the statistics of banknote issuance and cash reserves in various countries, the amount of banknotes issued last year decreased in the United States and Japan compared with 1933, except for a slight increase in the United Kingdom. And cash reserves have gradually increased. It can be seen that the main purpose of currency inflation is to devalue the currency, suppress the rate of increase, increase prices, and develop exports, not to issue banknotes indiscriminately.

From the perspective of the exchange rate, since 1931, the exchange rate of non-gold standard countries against France, a gold standard country, has consistently declined. The exchange rates between non-gold standard countries are affected by currency devaluation wars and other factors. In general, the exchange rate of the British pound against the U.S. dollar and the Japanese yen has been increasing since 1932. In 1934, due to the U.S. gold and silver nationalization policy, the exchange rate of the British pound against the U.S. dollar increased from 4.218 U.S. dollars in 1933 to 5.040. The exchange rate of the British pound against the Japanese yen also increased this year compared to the previous year. Looking at the exchange rate of the U.S. dollar against the Japanese yen, due to Japan's abandonment of the gold standard at the end of 1931, the exchange rate increased significantly in 1932 and 1933, putting Japan at a disadvantage in export trade competition. At the end of 1932 and the beginning of 1933, the exchange rate of the U.S. dollar against the Japanese yen increased to two U.S. dimes for one Japanese yen. In March 1933, the U.S. abandoned the gold standard, and the exchange rate gradually decreased. By July of the same year, it had decreased to 2.8 U.S. dimes for one Japanese yen. After October, until May 1934, it decreased to three dimes due to the U.S. gold policy. Therefore, the average exchange rate of the U.S. dollar against the Japanese yen in 1934 was 0.2971 U.S. dollars, which was lower than 0.2565 U.S. dollars in 1923. (To be continued)

National Doctors' Day Commemorative Special Issue

The Causes and Consequences of March 17th 174

— Guo Boliang

In the 17th year of the Republic of China, the surge of anger against the abolition of traditional Chinese medicine at the Health Committee meeting erupted. My colleagues in the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Association (now the National Medicine Association) were the first to fight for it. Subsequently, at the request of medical groups across the country, we initiated the organization of a national conference of representatives of medical and pharmaceutical groups to seek a way to preserve ourselves. Therefore, in view of the poor environment for traditional Chinese medicine, medical groups in Shanghai jointly initiated and convened a national conference of representatives of medical and pharmaceutical groups in Shanghai. On March 17th, when the meeting was held, representatives from seventeen provinces traveled thousands of miles to participate in the discussions. We gathered together to seek unity, to make effective arguments with righteous appeals. Therefore, the resolution to ban Chinese medicine in the 19th year of the Republic of China was not implemented. Time flies, and eight years have passed in an instant. Our traditional Chinese medicine has resisted cultural and economic aggression from abroad and sought academic progress and theoretical innovation internally, gradually moving towards a scientific path. The numerous achievements are obvious to all. On the occasion of the emergence of the March 17th National Doctors' Day, I dare to solemnly inform my beloved 450 million compatriots that traditional Chinese medicine has protected the health of the people, preserved national essence, and promoted culture for thousands of years, which is not without merit. Moreover, our eastern neighbor Japan is still reviving Chinese herbal medicine, and Western countries are also exploring Chinese medicine. It can be seen that traditional Chinese medicine has its true value, which our people should recognize. I have one more word to say to all medical circles across the country: All academics regress if they do not advance, and the same is true for our medical and pharmaceutical circles. If we only seek temporary survival without striving for self-improvement, then things rot and worms grow, giving opponents an opportunity to take advantage. For the sake of serving society and preserving the glorious history of thousands of years, in accordance with the principle of survival of the fittest, the Chinese medicine community should conduct further and deeper research on Chinese medicine academics in order to achieve perfection and gain faith. We should also be vigilant about the conspiracies and strategies of those who oppose us and never succumb to them. Let all my fellow practitioners rise up. Then, the future of traditional Chinese medicine may be promising.

History of National Medicine 175

— Lu Shi'e

Chinese medicine originated with Emperor Yan Shennong. The "Huainanzi" records that Shennong tasted the flavors of hundreds of herbs and encountered seventy poisons in a single day, from which medicine emerged. It can be seen that there was no medicine before Shennong. Since Shennong ruled China, the suffering of the people began to rely on him for relief. However, at the beginning of its invention, medicine was extremely simple, relying on the properties of drugs to treat diseases, without knowing the organization of prescriptions, let alone the meaning of prescriptions. During the Shennong era, the medical techniques invented included not only drug treatment, but also Bianstone, moxibustion, nine needles, guidance, massage, and other methods, all due to differences in local weather, climate, customs, and diseases, so treatments varied with time, place, and disease. The "Inner Canon" says that diseases are treated differently in different places, all with the same result, because of the terrain. This is what it means.

For example, the eastern regions are all places of fish and salt, near the sea and water. Their people eat fish and like salt, and they are all comfortable in their places, enjoying their food. Fish makes people hot, and salt overcomes blood, so their people are all black and sparse-skinned, and their diseases are mostly hemorrhoids. Hemorrhoids are caused by blood heat, and the best treatment for blood heat is Bianstone. Bianstone is a stone needle, a kind of magnetic peak. The mountains of the Gao clan have stones like jade, which can be used as needles. This is Bianstone, so the treatment with Bianstone comes from the east.

The west is a land of gold and jade, a place of sand and stone. Their people live on hills and are often windy, and the water and soil are strong. Their people do not wear clothes but wear rough cloth, eat extravagantly, and are fat. Evil cannot harm their bodies, and their diseases arise from within. Their treatment is suitable for poisons, so the treatment with poisons comes from the west.

The north is high and hilly, with wind, cold, and ice. Their people enjoy living in the wild and eating milk, and their cold storage often causes full-body diseases. Their treatment is suitable for moxibustion, which is the use of artemisia moxa and fire to burn, so the treatment with moxibustion comes from the north.

The south is low-lying, with weak and humid soil, and a gathering place for mist and dew. Their people like sour foods and eat rotten things, so their people are all fine-skinned and red, and they suffer from numbness. Their treatment is most suitable for fine needles, so the treatment with nine needles comes from the south.

The central land is flat and humid, and its people eat a variety of foods and do not labor, so their diseases are often weakness, faintness, chills, and fever. Their treatment is suitable for guidance and massage, so the techniques of guidance and massage come from the center.

The five treatments of national medicine were all invented during the Shennong era. Since Xuanyuan Huangdi conquered the unrighteous with martial virtue and ruled China in place of Shennong, he gathered the heroes of the four directions and discussed them in the Mingtang. Qi Bo, Lei Gong, Bo Gao, and others freely debated, and the methods of diagnosing diseases, such as feeling the pulse, observing the color, listening to the sound, and asking questions, were greatly improved. The muscles, skin, tendons, bones, meridians, collaterals, viscera, Yingwei qi, and blood flow, the wells, springs, ying, yu, and combining points were all made clear, and the book "Inner Canon" was written, which is the ancestor of medical books.

The Shang minister Yi Yin, who assisted Tang and ruled the world, paid attention to the people's diseases and collected medical prescriptions widely, writing the book "Tangye Jing", which is the ancestor of medical prescription books.

Chunyu Yi, the Han Taicang public, responded to the call of Emperor Wen and treated various symptoms with his hands, listing twenty-four cases, and presented them to the court, becoming the ancestor of national medical case records.

The late teacher Zhang Zhongjing, during the reign of Emperor Ling of the Eastern Han Dynasty, lamented that doctors at the time each inherited family skills and did not seek to understand the classics. When encountering heatstroke, they arbitrarily treated with cold water, and for cold symptoms, they used fire to chase away warmth, resulting in successive deaths. The Zhang surname clan was usually large, but two-thirds of them died in ten years, with typhoid fever accounting for seven out of ten deaths. Grieving the loss of the past and lamenting the irredeemable death, he developed unique methods of treatment, distinguishing between the meridians and differentiating symptoms, clearly distinguishing between cold and heat, establishing 397 methods and compiling 113 formulas, which became the southern needle for the treatment of exogenous diseases and also covered the treatment of miscellaneous diseases.

Since Zhongjing, the famous families of the Tang dynasties Sun Simiao and Wang Xi, the four great families of the Jin and Yuan dynasties Liu, Li, Zhang, and Zhu, the Beibei of the Ming dynasties Li and Qi Jingyue, and the various famous families of the Qing dynasties Qi, Xue, Wu, and Wang, although they talked about fire, yin, dampness, and heat, focusing on the spleen, kidney, and the gate of life, they were all different, but they were only supplementing Zhongjing.

More than 130 people have annotated Zhongjing's books before and after, each with their own opinions, inevitably biased, but only Qingxian Wujin Zou Ruanan was the only one who truly recognized the true purpose of the Treatise on Febrile Diseases.

It has been nearly five thousand years since Shennong, so national medicine has a history of five thousand years, making it the crown of the world's learning. From Shennong to Huangdi was the era of medical invention, and until Zhang Zhongjing of the Eastern Han Dynasty emerged, academics were fully prepared. From the Tang and Song dynasties to the present, various great families and famous families have only supplemented Zhongjing's theory. This is the history of national medicine.

Expectations for National Doctors' Day 176

— Yang Yanhe

A guest asked me, "Is March 17th the birthday of Xuanyuan or Qibo, or is it a memorial to Yaowang Jian Shanjun?" I said, "No, no." He said, "Then why is National Doctors' Day set on this day? Is there any explanation?" I said, "Yes, yes. This day is the day in the 18th year of the Republic of China when medical and pharmaceutical circles across the country held a conference of representatives in opposition to the abolition of traditional Chinese medicine. It is now designated as National Doctors' Day, probably because we want to base ourselves on the spirit of struggle from the past and make continuous efforts in the future." However, time does not stay, and six years have passed in an instant. Reviewing the past events, there are things that cause people to feel emotional. On March 22nd of the 18th year, the Shen Bao published an interview with Health Minister Xue Ziliang, "...Currently, most of those engaged in traditional Chinese medicine, except for a few who are enlightened and far-sighted, are sticking to old ways and cannot conduct intensive research and progress. In this era of rapid scientific advancement, if we continue to err and do not catch up quickly, I am afraid that our knowledge will lag behind and we will inevitably be eliminated...In the future, in order to adjust the national economy and improve Chinese medicine, we should guide those engaged in traditional Chinese medicine to study anatomy, physiology, chemistry, pathology, pharmacology, and other subjects separately, and systematically organize the existing medical classics..." However, for six years, those who stick to old ways are still sticking to old ways. The few national Chinese medicine schools, although they are slightly equipped with books on anatomy, physiology, chemistry, and other subjects, have never dissected corpses, and they have no chemical instruments, nor have they ever chemically tested drugs. The past six years are over. What about the next six years? We look forward to living up to Xue's words from the past and not failing the support of all walks of life at that time. Only then will we not be in vain for today's commemoration. Let us all strive together.

Why Commemorate March 17th 177

— Wu Quji

(Preface) I work as an editor at the Shenzhou National Medicine Association. I am not particularly famous. This time, our medical and pharmaceutical communities are holding a grand "March 17th" commemoration. The gentlemen at the meeting asked me to write an article for the association. I couldn't refuse, so I just casually said some nonsense. I seek the guidance of contemporary masters.

Someone asked me, "Today is March 17th on the Gregorian calendar. Is it your medical and pharmaceutical communities' memorial day?" I said, "Yes."

They further asked, "What is the significance of holding this memorial day?"

I said, "Haven't you seen the 'China-Centered Cultural Declaration' made by ten professors in the education sector recently? Doesn't that declaration contain these three sentences? (1) Review the past. (2) Grasp the present. (3) Create the future. The reason we are initiating the commemoration of this 'March 17th' festival is also this principle." He said, "I'd like to hear you explain this principle."

I said, "If you're not afraid of trouble, please listen to me explain it one by one."

(First) Review the Past. When it was 1929, some Western doctors wanted to test their scientific medical methods and advocated abolishing traditional Chinese medicine. We Shanghai comrades felt that this situation of signing the petition was not appropriate, so we immediately united and organized a National Federation of Medical and Pharmaceutical Organizations. It was established on March 17th of that year. On one hand, we petitioned the government to preserve traditional medicine. On the other hand, we gathered comrades from home and abroad to fight together. At that time, there was a real sense of "a single call from a high place brings responses from all the mountains." In the end, traditional Chinese medicine was fortunately preserved. However, because the medical and pharmaceutical organizations were jointly organized, it was not in line with current laws. Therefore, the National Federation of Medical and Pharmaceutical Organizations was dissolved. Our medical and pharmaceutical communities suffered a setback from this, and countless forces were lost invisibly. This is something that deserves attention and cannot be ignored.

(Second) Grasp the Present. Since the dissolution of the National Federation of Medical and Pharmaceutical Organizations, the central government, although complying with public opinion, established a National Medicine Institute. However, its power was limited to academic research. It had no political influence. Last autumn, the gentlemen of the Legislative Yuan understood that our native medicine was indeed valuable and should not be neglected. They immediately passed a set of regulations for traditional Chinese medicine and sent it to the Executive Yuan. Due to certain reasons, this regulation is still on the books but not implemented. Comrades in the medical community have also submitted petitions and gone to the capital to petition, but still cannot get approval. So, our traditional Chinese medicine's political reliance is so weak, how can it still stand on its feet in society? What is the reason for this? Alas. We must understand that this is our self-reliance. Our self-reliance, on the medical side, is having the specialty of treating diseases. On the pharmaceutical side, it is that the medicines have incredible efficacy. These two facts are the real evidence of our self-reliance. Everyone must understand that the current era is an era of survival of the fittest. If we want to exist permanently, we must use our existing self-reliance and work hard practically.

(Third) Create the Future. The two words "create" are not easy to achieve. Moreover, medical and pharmaceutical matters are especially difficult. But our country has an idiom: "Nothing is difficult in the world for one who sets his mind to it." Napoleon I of France also said, "The word 'difficult' does not exist in the French dictionary." Our medical and pharmaceutical communities have experienced many storms in recent years, and we have all realized something. Therefore, we often hear discussions about reorganizing Chinese medicine. This is a very gratifying thing. I think that reorganizing our country's medicine requires written work, which is indispensable. The most important thing is grassroots work. Why? Written work is only for explaining the truth of our medicine and spreading the effectiveness of our treatments. This is academic research, and ordinary people are not interested in it. What they need is to be able to be cured by a doctor immediately when they get sick. This is what they welcome most. Our medicine has already gained the faith of the people. If we put a lot of effort into grassroots work, so that people in society all feel that they must use their own medicine for treatment, then our foundation will be solid. Even if others want to overthrow it, they will have no way to do so.

My feelings about March 17th are like this. Do you think it's right?

That person listened, nodded, smiled, and didn't say a word, then walked away.

So I wrote down this conversation as my article. Please forgive me and give me your guidance.

Hopes for the Future of the Medical and Pharmaceutical Communities 178

— Yu Tongfang

The March 17th "National Medicine Day." The six medical and pharmaceutical organizations in this city jointly held a commemorative meeting and plan to gradually implement the plan. This is truly a sign of the revival of Chinese medicine and a movement for national health. For the past twenty years, our country's medicine has suffered greatly due to external forces invading and seizing the leading position. It has been difficult to make significant progress in development. This is truly due to the pressure of the situation. Looking at countries around the world, they are all researching Chinese medicine as a newly discovered treasure and purchasing Chinese medicinal materials to make new drugs, which are then resold to our country. The outflow of profits is countless. Today, rural areas are declining, cities are desolate, lost territories have not been recovered, and the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent. Now that the medical and pharmaceutical colleagues are jointly holding the March 17th "National Medicine Day" commemorative meeting, I dare to offer my sincere suggestions and express my hopes. I hope that it will be implemented gradually and achieve success. Tongfang cannot help but offer a fragrant prayer.

(A) Hopes for the Medical Community

(1) Medical skills are inherently benevolent arts. Those who founded this profession took "social policies for governing the country and saving the people" as their fundamental aim. Physics theory states, "Doctors should not be entrusted without benevolence, cannot be relied upon without intelligence and reason, and cannot be trusted without integrity and purity." Therefore, in the future, academic research should diligently seek ancient teachings and widely adopt new knowledge. Treatment should have remarkable results to show. Find ways to cure diseases that foreign medicine cannot cure. If one person's strength is not enough, then combine the strength of several people or use the strength of a group. Impose compassion for the poor and reduce consultation fees or provide them completely free of charge to conform to the original meaning of the benevolent art.

(2) Deeply believe that traditional Chinese medicine has real efficacy in treatment. Do not be tempted by external forces. Do not make fence-sitting arguments. Adhere to the original intention of "studying national medicine for the sake of national medicine." Hold the belief of "doing national medicine for the sake of national medicine." Smile and nod at those who slander us. Smile and nod at those who praise us. The so-called "facts speak louder than words." There is no need to defend ourselves, and even less to boast.

(3) Traditional Chinese medicine has outstanding efficacy. It should be vigorously promoted to make it known to every household. Provide guidance on hygiene everywhere, whether it is public hygiene or personal hygiene, disease prevention, before and after illness, all should be paid attention to. Do not rely on one prescription to finish the matter. Should be fully responsible.

(B) Hopes for the Pharmaceutical Community

(1) Medicines are for treating diseases. Even with good doctors, if there are no good medicines, medicine is useless. Doctors and medicines are as closely related as lips and teeth. Should support each other for common survival and prosperity. Do not be greedy for huge profits and use fake products to confuse the real ones. Decoction should follow ancient methods. Do not simplify them due to crudeness and simplicity and ruin your reputation. And hope that you will each report on each other and supervise each other, and hold firm beliefs.

(2) Each province has different soil and climates, producing different medicines. Each medicine has its own bias in medicinal properties, and each treatment uses its own. Therefore, when discussing medicine, the first priority is authenticity. Do not misattribute or substitute one for another. This will disrupt the individuality of national medicine and lose its therapeutic effect.

In summary, these points are easy to implement, but must be persisted in to see their effectiveness. The most important thing is that our medical and pharmaceutical communities should unite, help each other, truly connect with each other, and jointly strategize to implement relevant policies in order to break through this difficult situation and reach a bright path. Do you all agree?

— Xu Xiangren

Written for the 24th March 17th Commemoration

Is it in business, or in status? These are all matters for one person at one time and have nothing to do with the overall situation. In my opinion, the only way out for our national medicine is to work together on academics, have precise achievements, and gain the trust of good people. All my comrades, quickly rise up and plan for it.

Junior Cup Final; Donghua B Wins the Championship; A Decisive 3-0 Victory Over Xibu B; Excellent Performance Beyond Expectations 181

Donghua B and Xibu B competed in the final of the Xilian Football Junior Cup at Yiyuan yesterday. Donghua unexpectedly defeated Xibu 3-0 and won the championship. Donghua won due to its balanced talent, excellent offense and defense, and skilled coordination. Xibu was extremely disorganized, with no cooperation, relying entirely on their burly physique, which was exploited by Donghua. Only a few hundred spectators watched yesterday.

A Sigh of Regret for the Penalty Kick

Xibu kicked off, and Donghua launched an attack on Xibu with clever short passes. They were active in front of Xibu's goal, but Xibu used their tall bodies to head and shoulder barge, trying everything. After repeated attempts failed, Donghua's momentum waned slightly. Then Xibu launched a heavy attack, which was fierce, and Donghua was worried for a while. After about half an hour of back and forth, Wu Binghao led his troops to Xibu's goal, deep into their territory. Seeing the situation was not good, Douglas tackled, but violated Article 9 and was penalized with a penalty kick. Everyone was overjoyed, and Chen Yutian took the kick. He used too little force, and the ball was too low and was saved by the goalkeeper. The whole field sighed with regret.

Wu Binghao Scores the First Goal

Chen Yutian missed a good opportunity, so everyone hoped that he could redeem himself. Ten minutes after missing the penalty kick, Zhang Jinhai was more than ten yards from the goal and took a shot. Alan stretched his foot to block it, resulting in a corner kick. Chen Yutian was an experienced corner kicker, and his placement was accurate and just right. Wu Binghao took a shot from behind and scored into the goal. The Xibu goal, which was not easy to break, finally fell. Although Xibu desperately counterattacked, Donghua led 1-0 in the first half.

Donghua Leads 2-0

After switching sides in the second half, Xibu tried their best to counterattack, but lacking shooting skills and clever coordination, they relied only on their clumsy hard work, which was naturally useless. Donghua defended firmly, moved when the opportunity arose, and attacked and defended each other. After holding out for half an hour, Donghua's center forward Gong Ziwen dribbled straight in. Xibu was recklessly attacking, leaving the defense empty. Gong charged forward, and Alan rushed out to stop him. Marius hurriedly ran in to replace him. Seeing Alan, he quickly passed to Wu Binghao, who took a shot at the goal. Marius was also shot down. At this point, Donghua led 2-0.

Chen Yutian Creates a 3-0 Lead

Donghua's victory was certain. Xibu's counterattack was just a formality. With three minutes left in the game, Donghua scored a third goal unexpectedly. Xibu put all their efforts into the attack, completely ignoring their defense. Qin Zuozi got the ball and dribbled straight in, passing to Chen Yutian on the right. Chen took a shot at the goal, making it 3-0 and securing the victory.

Zilin Cup Final; Youyou's Miserable Defeat is a Pity; St. Francis Wins the Championship 3-2; Yang Mingjin Injured and Leaves the Game 182

Yesterday afternoon, Youyou B and St. Francis competed in the final of the Zilin Cup at Zhongyuan Stadium. There were few spectators, only three or four hundred, just for decoration. However, the shouts from the east and west were quite lively. Judging from yesterday's battle, the two teams were evenly matched, and their strength was very equal, making the competition intense. However, Youyou's goalkeeper injured his leg and left the game halfway. St. Francis took the opportunity to attack and finally won the Zilin Cup 3-2. The situation at the time is recorded below.

Shi Qi Opens the Scoring

With three rings of the bell and the referee's order, the battle broke out. Youyou took advantage of the weather and its flags were often in St. Francis' territory, attacking horizontally and vertically. St. Francis accepted the attacks passively and defended carefully. Twenty minutes passed in the blink of an eye. Xi Qiaosheng intercepted a ball and sent it to the enemy's goal. Hu Youcheng was tripped by the enemy and could not shoot. Seeing the opportunity, Shen Shiqi rushed to the spot and, with a bang, the ball entered from the lower left corner, opening the scoring.

Penalty Kick

After Youyou won a goal, the forwards continued to show off their power and attack arbitrarily. Hu Youcheng got the ball at 20 yards and fired, certain to score. However, he was too impatient, and the ball went over the crossbar. St. Francis resolved the crisis and then took the opportunity to attack. Center forward Peterson got the ball and shot hard. Goalkeeper Yang caught it, but the enemy's forwards surged up and surrounded Yang. Yang wanted to avoid the enemy and slipped accidentally, suffering a heavy blow to his leg and falling to the ground. He had no choice but to leave the field, and Xu Wenkui replaced him. Before long, Koumani picked up a ball from the sideline, just in front of the goal. Goalkeeper Xu calmly jumped up to catch it, but the referee's silver whistle screamed wildly. For some reason, a penalty kick was awarded. Peterson took the kick and scored. The audience clamored non-stop. The first half ended in a 1-1 tie.

Peterson Scores Again

The second half started, and goalkeeper Yang endured the pain to assist in the battle. The competition between the two sides became more intense. St. Francis's right winger crossed the ball, and Peterson arrived without stopping, getting the ball and shooting. Goalkeeper Yang staggered to guard the goal, and jumping was very inconvenient. He watched helplessly as the ball went into the net. St. Francis led 2-1, and Yang's injured leg became even more painful, making it difficult to support him. He had no choice but to leave the field again, and Shi Jinsheng replaced him.

Becomes a 3-1 Score

St. Francis became more and more courageous. Youyou was a crippled army, leaving them to attack at will. St. Francis's right winger dribbled quickly, and at the appropriate point, shot hard at the goal, accurately and quickly, scoring again and making it 3-1.

Ends 3-2

Although they lost in the east, they could make up for it in the west. Youyou, stimulated by this, used their entire army, with a do-or-die spirit, furiously attacking St. Francis's territory. Finally, Xu Wenkui scored a goal, and the audience applauded thunderously. Encouraged by this, Youyou's attack became even stronger. Just as they were about to turn the tide, a long whistle announced the end. The lineups of both sides are as follows:

International Lawn Tennis Association; Specifies the Number of Voting Rights for Each Country 186

(Havas News Agency, Paris, 15th) The International Lawn Tennis Association held a meeting today to amend Article 16 of the Articles of Association regarding the voting rights of tennis associations in each member country. The new article specifies the voting rights of each country as follows: Germany, Australia, the United States, France, and the United Kingdom each get 12 votes. Canada, Japan, Italy, New Zealand, the South African Federation, and the Czech Republic each get 10 votes. Austria, Belgium, Denmark, the Netherlands, and Switzerland each get 7 votes. Argentina, Egypt, Spain, Finland, Greece, Hungary, India, Southern Ireland, Norway, and Sweden each get 5 votes. Brazil, Bulgaria, Chile, Columbia, Cuba, Ecuador, Estonia, Mexico, Monaco, Paraguay, Peru, Portugal, Romania, Uruguay, Venezuela, and Yugoslavia each get 3 votes. The Dutch East Indies and British East Africa each get 1 vote.

Sponsored by the Wuhan Sports Association: Central China Basketball and Soccer Tournament 190

Tournament Date Set for April 1st to 7th; Invitations Sent to Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi Provinces to Participate Enthusiastically

(Hankou Dispatch) The Wuhan Sports Association, to promote sports in the Central China provinces, is sponsoring the Central China Regional Men's and Women's Basketball and Men's Soccer Championships. The competition rules and dates have been finalized, and on the 15th, letters were sent to the education departments of Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces, inviting them to select outstanding athletes and participate enthusiastically. The original letter and rules are as follows:

Official Letter: We believe that the strength of the national physique is related to the rise and fall of the nation. Education authorities, aware of this, have vigorously promoted sports in recent years, and the atmosphere is becoming increasingly vibrant. However, compared to other regions, the Central China provinces lag behind. After investigating the reasons, we find that they are no more than the following two: (1) lack of effective promotion organizations or groups; (2) lack of opportunities for mutual learning and observation. Therefore, at the first meeting of the Standing Committee of this Association, it was resolved to send letters to the Central China provinces, proposing to hold the Central China Regional Men's and Women's Basketball and Men's Soccer Championships in Hankou during the spring break this year, so that athletes from the four provinces can have the opportunity to learn from and observe each other, making the sports atmosphere more intense and arousing public interest in sports. We have long admired your department's enthusiasm in promoting sports, and we believe that you will support and participate in this event, contributing to its success. Now, we enclose a copy of the competition rules for participation by the provinces, which is sent with this letter. Please investigate and reply by telegram for planning and implementation purposes.

Rules: (1) The tournament is named the Central China Regional Basketball and Soccer Championship; (2) The Central China region is defined as Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces; (3) The events are divided into men's and women's basketball and men's soccer, with two championship trophies awarded. This year, the Wuhan Sports Association initiates and is responsible for hosting the event; (4) The date of the event is set during the spring break this year, from April 1st to 7th; (5) The location is in Wuhan this year; (6) Each unit should send the list of athletes by registered mail before March 28th; (7) Each unit must register in Hankou before April 2nd; (8) The number of athletes is ten per men's basketball team, twelve per women's team, and fifteen per soccer team; (9) The number of staff is one head of delegation per province, and one instructor and one manager per team; (10) The Association is responsible for bidding for accommodation and meals for each unit. Each province is responsible for its own transportation costs; (11) The competition system adopts a single round-robin system. The Association will be responsible for the overall planning and management of referees and all sports equipment. (15th)

Wife of Veteran Athlete Lu Ming Killed by Gunfire in Beiping 195

Shot Seven Times and Died on the Spot; Perpetrator Liu Jinggui, Formerly Engaged to Lu; Teng Was a Good Shot Putter, Basketball, and Volleyball Player

An Unprecedented Bloody Case of a Love Triangle Among Athletes

(Beiping, 16th) At around 10 a.m. this morning, at the Tongzhi Girls' Middle School in Fangsheng Hutong, Beiping City, a female guest named Liu Jinggui, under the pseudonym Li Zhenhua, visited Teng Shuang, a female physical education teacher. After being received, Liu and Teng met, and after only a few words, Liu pulled out a pistol and fired seven shots at Teng, all hitting vital points. Teng died on the spot. The perpetrator, Liu Jinggui, surrendered on the spot and was taken into custody by the police. According to Liu's confession, she is 24 years old, from Yihua, Chahar Province, and studied at the Beihua Art School. She did not know Teng. Because after she became engaged to Lu Ming, Teng took away her fiancé Lu Ming, causing her to suffer greatly. She originally planned to kill Lu Ming, but realized that a single woman's ability was limited, so she decided to put Teng to death. Lu originally had a wife. After meeting her in 1932, she asked him to divorce his wife first, but Lu did not agree. Then, at the North China Games that year, he met Teng Shuang. Lu took a job at Lihua Middle School, and Teng asked Lu to divorce his wife. Lu divorced his wife in 1932. In November, he paid her 600 yuan, saying that he was severing previous relationships. She had no way to deal with it and could only endure the pain. In April of that year, Lu married Teng in Yihua. She killed Teng this time to avenge her for destroying her relationship with Lu Ming. The pistol was bought from a rickshaw puller, etc. Dai Ming is a veteran in the sports world and currently works at the Xiahuayuan Station on the PingSui Railway. Because the deceased and the perpetrator are both related to Lu Ming, the authorities sent a letter to the Xiahuayuan Station on the PingSui Railway in Yihua, summoning him to come to the case for questioning.

Brief History of Teng Shuang

Ms. Teng Shuang is from Shaoyang, Hunan, and graduated from Beiping Normal University. She is also an athletic star. She won the shot put championship at the North China Games and was a basketball and volleyball star in Beiping. She was selected for the Beiping basketball team at the 4th National Games in Hangzhou. At the 5th National Games in Nanjing, Ms. Teng served as the manager of the Beiping team. She is the older sister of Teng Shugu, a reporter for the Shishi Daily. Mr. Teng was very saddened upon receiving the news and decided to go to Beiping today to investigate the truth.

Middle School Students from this City Hold Mandarin Speech Contest Preliminary Today 199

Starting at 8:00 AM at Wuben Girls' Middle School; Junior and Senior High School Contestants Start at the Same Time

The Mandarin speech contest for middle school students in this city, sponsored by the National Mandarin Education Promotion Association, is scheduled to be held at Wuben Girls' Middle School at 8:00 AM today for preliminary rounds. Approximately one hundred people have registered to participate. Junior and senior high school students will compete simultaneously, and the event will conclude in the morning. Details are as follows:

Judging Groups: The judging will be divided into six groups, with four people in each group, each responsible for one item. The list of judges is as follows: Group 1: Tong Xingbai, Wang Fuquan, Ma Guoying, Yan Gongshang; Group 2: Chen Bai, Zhang Yongshu, Li Weiyu, Chen Dabei; Group 3: Jiang Jianbai, Zhou Shang, Zu Bingren, Xu Gongmei; Group 4: Xie Liuyi, Hu Quanyi, Xu Kuibo, Li Huazhi; Group 5: Cao Juren, Zhao Jingshen, Pei Weisen, Jin Guangmei; Group 6: Chen Zizhan, Xu Maoyong, Le Sibing, Wang Gongxia.

Scoring Method: The substance is divided into four items: thought (15 points), structure (15 points), vocabulary (10 points), grammar (10 points), totaling 50 points. The form is divided into four items: voice (15 points), intonation (15 points), expression (10 points), action (10 points), totaling 50 points. Each item is divided into three grades: excellent, above average, and average. For thought, structure, voice, and intonation, 1 to 5 points are average, 6 to 10 points are above average, and 11 to 15 points are excellent. For vocabulary, grammar, expression, and action, 1 point is excellent.

Initiated by the Chinese Cultural Construction Association: The Reading Movement is Gradually Becoming Concrete 201

The Competitive Association's Preparations Have Been Completed; The Books Have Been Selected by Experts; Registration Begins on the 20th

The reading movement fully supported by the Chinese Cultural Construction Association is now gradually becoming concrete. The first step is to establish a Reading Competitive Association. The chairman of the association, Wu Xingya, has convened five meetings to discuss all the progress. In addition to the results of the first three meetings, which have been reported in the press, we now report on the latest situation as follows:

Selected Books

The Reading Competitive Association is divided into university and middle school groups. Each group must select several types of books as textbooks and reference books. However, because it is very difficult to select books, the preparatory committee specially hired Wu Xingya, Li Ximou, Zhu Kezhen, Gao Yihan, Chen Lifu, Cai Yuanpei, Pan Gongzhan, Liu Binglin and others as book selection committee members. The books that have been selected are as follows: (A) University Group: (1) The Three Principles of the People, the Outline of National Construction, the Strategies of National Construction (Reference book: the Draft Constitution of the Republic of China compiled by the Legislative Yuan, Chen Lifu's "On Vitalism"); (2) Chen Ronglu's "Modern History of China" (Reference book: Xia Zengyou's "Ancient History of China"); (3) Lin Guangcheng's translation of "The New World Situation"; (4) Wang Xinggong's "Introduction to Science"; (5) Sun Hanbing's "Political Science and Government" (Reference book: Wang Shijie's "Comparative Constitution"); (6) Wang Jianzu's translation of "Kidd's Economics" (Reference book: Yan Fu's translation of "The Wealth of Nations", Wang Kaihua's translation of "National Economics"); (7) Zhang Dongsun's "Philosophy" (Reference book: Feng Youlan's "History of Chinese Philosophy") (B) Middle School Group: (1) The Three Principles of the People (Reference books: Tao Baichuan's "An Outline of the Three Principles of the People", Lou Tongsun's "Research on the Three Principles of the People"); (2) Luo Wenkun's "Kaiming High School Textbook of National History" (Reference book: Lu Simian's "Vernacular National History"); (3) Zhang Qiyun's "Commercial Press New School System High School Textbook of National Geography" (Reference book: Wang Qinpei's "Modern Geography"); (4) Ren Hongjun's "Introduction to Natural Science"; (5) Sa Mengwu's "Introduction to Politics" (Reference book: Pan Chuji's); (6) Tu Xiaoshi's "Outline of Famous Learning" (Reference book: Chen Gaoyong's "Outline of Famous Learning")

Reading Method

The first phase of reading will last from April to October. Anyone who wishes to participate in reading must register with the local Cultural Construction Association on the 20th of this month. The registration period is one month. Anyone who registers to join the association will be given a cheap book purchase coupon, which can be used to purchase the above-mentioned books from bookstores at half price or even lower.

Correspondence Guidance

Anyone participating in the Reading Competitive Association can ask questions about the books by correspondence. After receiving the letter, the association will forward it to the specialized instructors for separate replies. The instructors who have been hired include Li Ximou and others. Several more people will be hired in the future to be responsible for explaining difficulties.

Assigned Staff

The preparatory committee decided to appoint several people to assist the chairman in handling daily affairs in order to ensure that the reading movement spreads throughout the country. Wu Xingya, chairman of the committee, has now appointed Jiang Jianbai as the general manager, Wang Xinming as the general secretary, and Zhou Hanmei and Huang Jingzhai as secretaries.

Expand Publicity

In order to create a good atmosphere for learning and encourage young people across the country to join this reading association, the association plans to expand the publicity of the reading movement. Many methods have been determined, and a large number of slogans have been printed for posting. The most incisive slogans are as follows: (1) In school, you must study hard, and when you buy a book, you must read it; (2) Save the wasted time to read; (3) Using both hands and brains is a great thing; (4) Not only students should read, but also teachers should read.
