Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

China Needs Machines to Manufacture Machines 211

— Xi Shi

Children! Look, isn't China now striving for productive construction? The raw materials and machinery needed for productive construction – raw materials are the most abundant in China. If you use your two eyes! And your hands to find them, they are everywhere, but what about machinery? Machinery is the most important tool in productive construction. We need many kinds of machinery, but which kind of machinery do we need the most?

The machinery we need most is machines to manufacture machines. The reason for this is very clear, because if we have this kind of machinery, we can manufacture all other kinds of machinery. In our country, we only have airplanes, but we don't have machines to manufacture airplanes; in our country, we only have automobiles, but we don't have machines to manufacture automobiles; there are so many examples like this. Therefore, we have to buy them from foreign countries.

Children, use your clever minds and lively hands to work hard to prepare to manufacture machines to manufacture machines.

A Patriotic Child 212

— Ling

Wang'er was a child of bright intelligence and lively movements. Unfortunately, his father passed away due to illness when he was four years old. Therefore, his mother did some needlework and barely managed to support herself and Wang'er. In the blink of an eye, Wang'er was thirteen years old. His mother's health was declining day by day, and she could no longer do much needlework. She wanted to find something for Wang'er to do to maintain their livelihood, so she asked people everywhere to help find a job for her son. But she searched for a month, two months, three months... but found nothing. So his mother became anxious. One quiet night, she tossed and turned, unable to sleep. In the rustling sound of the breeze blowing through the treetops, she thought of a plan: to sell newspapers. Later, she decided on this plan. Before the sun rose, she told her son about the plan, and her son agreed. So his mother said many kind words and borrowed some money from the neighbors as capital to sell newspapers. From that day on, Wang'er went out every day to make a living. Even in heavy rain and cold wind, he had to keep running.

After a few years, the country had a war against foreign powers. He still did his job every day. He also knew a few characters, so when he saw the blood-red characters printed on the newspaper every day, he was shocked. After he had finished distributing the newspaper every day, he sat in the corner, looking at the newspaper very uncomfortably. Although he did not know many characters, he already knew that China was being invaded by imperialism. In his simple mind, he wanted to join the army. Later, as the war gradually intensified, he abandoned his job, left his beloved mother, and went to the front lines. So every day he and his comrades resisted and fought on the battlefield. Unfortunately, a ferocious bomb entered his patriotic heart, and he sacrificed himself. He sacrificed himself for the country! In the whirring sound of airplanes and the booming sound of artillery, he was faintly heard shouting "Long live the Republic of China, long live, long live...!"

Similarities between Animals and Plants 213

— Bing Yu

The animals like cats and dogs, and plants like flowers, grasses, and trees that you usually see seem to have very different lives. However, in reality, the natures of animals and plants are the same. First, both plants and animals have parents. When a plant blooms with beautiful flowers, its stamen pollen is blown into the pistil, which will produce seeds. Second, both animals and plants breathe. If plants lack oxygen, they will wither and die. Animals stop breathing and suffocate to death immediately. If we look through a microscope, plants have countless small holes, breathing non-stop. Third, both animals and plants eat. Animals eat through their mouths, and plants absorb from their roots, trunks, branches, and leaves. Fourth, animals and plants each have weapons of resistance. Humans use punches and kicks, cats and dogs use claws and teeth to grab and bite, and the fine needles and thorns of plants such as cacti and poppy are all for resisting harm. Fifth, plants also quarrel. When weeds spread wildly and hinder nearby plants, irises will curl up their stems and break the weeds. Sixth, animals love their children, and plants also protect their seeds, like the fruit of coconuts and the thorns of chestnuts. Seventh, both animals and plants need to rest. We get up in the morning and sleep at night, and plants absorb nutrients during the day and stop working to rest when the sun sets. Eighth, both animals and plants have the function of metabolism. The hair, skin, and cells of animals grow and fall off all year round, and the roots, branches, leaves, and bark of plants also often wither and are replaced. From this point of view, animals are tangible dynamic actions, and plants are intangible static changes. The natures of the two are completely the same.

Who Works Hard? 214

— Written by Zhang Shuhe, Age Nine

Snail and Ming'er 215

— Jin Xi

Ming'er is a fifth-grade student at Lizhi Elementary School. His memory is very poor, and his understanding is also worse than others. Therefore, he cannot keep up with his classmates in all subjects.

The teacher advised him to work hard patiently, and several playful classmates gave him the nickname "Dumb Bug." Ming'er accepted the teacher's advice and inevitably felt ashamed and angry at the students' ridicule.

One day, Ming'er was taking a walk in the garden when he unintentionally saw a snail struggling to climb up the base of an earthen wall. The snail's crawling speed was very slow. So much time had passed, and it still had not crawled even a foot.

Ming'er couldn't help but laugh and ask, "Snail! Are you a dumb bug like me? You crawl so slowly, do you still want to climb to the top of the wall?" But the snail didn't say a word and just kept moving forward.

In the evening, Ming'er came to see the snail again. To Ming'er's surprise, the snail had already climbed high to the top of the wall. It was as if the snail was answering Ming'er with facts: "Don't be discouraged, crawl patiently, crawl tirelessly, and even a dumb bug can climb to the top of the wall."

After being moved by this, Ming'er patiently, diligently, and tirelessly studied all subjects. He used his hard work to make up for his shortcomings in understanding and memory. In less than a few months, every teacher praised him, and the students no longer dared to call him "Dumb Bug."

How Do Plants Survive Winter? 216

— He Gongchao

Plants need two things to survive: a suitable temperature and proper moisture. In winter, the temperature is low and the air is very dry. The ground is sometimes frozen, and there is no way to absorb water. Therefore, many plants wither and die. But in the spring, they will still grow or come back to life. Like balsam flowers, they leave behind seeds before they wither, and these seeds will regrow when the weather gets warm (Figure 1). Some plants have stems and leaves that wither, but their roots in the soil are still alive. When the weather turns warm next year, new stems and leaves will grow from these roots; chrysanthemums are like this (Figure 2). Those trees, although their leaves have fallen, their branches and trunks are still alive. When the weather warms up, new buds will grow (Figure 3). Pine, cypress, evergreen, and holly are considered the strongest plants. Their leaves do not wither in winter and are still green and verdant (Figure 4).

If we want to have beautiful trees, we must protect them in winter: flower and grass seeds should be stored in glass bottles, ready to be sown when the weather warms up. For plants with roots left in the ground, use rice husks, ash, and straw to cover the roots to keep them warm. The branches and trunks should be tied with straw to avoid damage from frost, snow, and cold air (Figure 5). If we protect trees, flowers, and grasses in this way, our gardens will surely become lively again when the weather warms up.

The Origin of Felt 217

— Linghu Zhao

Children, do you know the origin of felt? The origin of felt has an interesting history of discovery.

Hundreds of years ago, there was a foreign traveling monk named Clement. One day, he was traveling to a high mountain; the mountain top was piled with a lot of white snow and yellow sand. It was not easy to walk over this mountain. He was afraid of hurting his feet, so he took two pieces of wool and lined them inside his shoes in advance.

When he walked over the mountain, the bottoms of his feet felt hot, so he took out the wool and took a look. What? The wool had turned into a kind of natural fabric. From then on, the traveling monk came up with the felt-making industry.

Little friends, although felt looks very much like a kind of fabric, it is not woven. The method of making felt is very simple. We only need to press the wool layer by layer so that its fibers overlap each other, and the felt can be made immediately.

Words with Wings 218

— Yang Hongfu

One day, when my younger brother and I were sitting under a large tree, we suddenly saw a small bird flying into the top of the tree. Later: the little bird sang a song, and after he finished singing that very nice song, he flew away with his wings! We wanted to go see that little bird again, but he had already used his small wings to fly away quickly.

Later we stood up to look at other birds and a bird's nest. Before long my brother saw a small thing fixed on a branch, he said: "That's a green little bird!" So I looked up and saw that it was a green frog, who was jumping from this branch to another branch. My brother looked and shouted: "Ah! He also has wings!"

Frogs' jump, is without wings, they have no wings. But birds have wings.

But "words" also have wings. If you don't hold them tightly, then they will immediately fly away!

Then: "How can you catch them?"

This method is very easy, just think often about their meanings, and be twelve minutes attentive to write and read them. In this way, they will live with you!

Mother's Education 219

— Yi An

Seesaw Candle 220

— Zi Xi

Ruizhen found a candle in the drawer and used a small knife to shave a little bit of the wick at the bottom. In the middle of the candle, she pierced a hole with an awl and passed a lead wire through the middle of the candle. The candle could rotate freely. She used another piece of wood with two bamboo pieces standing upright at both ends, with a circular shape shaved at the top. She inserted the lead wire in the middle and then tipped the heavier end down. She lit both ends of the wick with matches. Soon, the lower end would rise up, and after a while, the upper end would fall down again. From then on, moving up and down continuously, it became an automatic seesaw.

Just as Ruizhen was going crazy with excitement, her younger brother Ruizhang came too. Ruizhang watched for a long time and then excitedly asked her the reason.

Ruizhen stopped for a while and then said very proudly: "This is because the two sides cannot be balanced, and the heavier end will fall down. After lighting the two ends with fire, the candle at the falling end is melted more by the fire, and the heavier end becomes lighter and rises up, and the other side falls down. Moving up and down continuously in this way, isn't it the same as a seesaw?" Ruizhang was very impressed by his sister's intelligence.

Poor Dad 221

Whose New Life Is It? 222

— (Gu Pingdan)

Whose is the "New Life" promoted by Chairman Chiang?

I think: this new life does not belong to others, it is precisely ours, the children! Because new life is children, and children are new life.

How can we say that new life is children, and children are new life? It is not wrong at all, because children are born into this world lively, with new bodies, new brains, new vitality, new hope, new vitality… Living a new life in all of this newness, then, aren't children new life? Isn't new life children?

Since new life does not belong to others, but to children, then we children should implement our own new life in everything, so as not to fail the new life that we all have.

I wish: now is "Children's World," and the future will be "New Life World."

The Voyages of Sinbad the Sailor (10) 223

— Xin Qing

We slept on the beach in the evening, but were startled awake after a little while. I heard a sound nearby. This sound came from a large serpent as long as a palm tree, which had crept very close to us while we were asleep.

It seized one of my friends in its large jaws, and although this man was struggling for his life, shouting at the top of his voice, the serpent devoured him in a moment. Now that I had only one friend left, we were so terrified that we ran away, otherwise, I am afraid we would have provided the beast with a second meal.

I cried, "What dangers we are facing! When we first came to this beautiful island, we were filled with joy, thinking that we had escaped from that black giant, but unexpectedly we are now on the verge of death!"

We saw a tall tree, so we spent the night in the middle of the branches. Before dawn, the serpent found us again and ate my last friend from the branch he was sitting on.

At this time I was extremely afraid, like a dead man, and then I was very happy, because that beast had gone. As soon as it was light, I came down from the tree, but I did not know which road was safe. I first thought of ending my own life and being done with it, but I felt that life was still sweet, so I trusted in God and began to make a safe place for myself.

I took a large pile of branches and long wooden strips and made a tall fence around the tree I was in. I tied the ends of the wooden strips to the branches. Tonight I will hide in my fort.

I had just finished doing this when the serpent came again. It wound itself around the fence I had made, but could not get in to make trouble for me. So he

came down to ambush me, just like a cat ambushing a mouse. At dawn it left me and returned to its lair.

I was weak and sick, because the beast's breath made me sick. When the sun rose, I left the village and came down to the beach, hoping to end my life, but I felt that death was sweeter than living and being so afraid.

When I arrived at the beach, I saw a ship in the distance. I made a flag out of my turban and waved it back and forth, and at the same time made the air vibrate with my loud shouts.

I was very happy to see that the people on the ship had seen me, and soon a small boat was launched to pick me up. As soon as I got on the boat, I told them everything that had happened to me. Then those people gave me the best food and a new set of clothes, because all I had left were tattered rags.

After a few hours at sea, we arrived at the island of Sarabak. We moored the cable in the port. The people on the ship had come to trade, so they took out their packages of goods from the cabin to prepare for sale.

Spring Is Here 224

— Lu Er Yu

Look, spring is here!

Look, spring is here!

We must catch spring and not let her escape.

Look at the butterflies dancing, the orioles calling,

Look at the distant trees behind,

A kitten turns out,

He says "Wonderful... ha... wonderful... wonderful... ha... wonderful,

We must catch spring and not let her escape,

Children should study hard early!"

May Contract Speculation Begins: Overall Trend Remains Flat, with Minimal Price Fluctuations Considering Swap Calculations

Yesterday, trading in the May contract began, with the trend remaining flat. The Central Bank initially sold shillings, causing prices to rise then fall. Sassoon seized the opportunity to cover short positions at low prices. News that the Central Bank might repurchase April contracts early at par led to a rebound, but the market ultimately ended with a mediocre performance. Considering swap rates, offers came mostly from the long side, resulting in a very stable outcome. Initially, the overseas silver market saw British banks covering short positions. After closing, the Indian quote was still selling at a low of .0625. While American banks were long, forward silver prices narrowed by 1.5 to 2.5 percent. Exchange rates continued to rise. London gold fell by 1 shilling and 7.5 pence, stirring sentiment. Off-floor forward trading opened, immediately rising to 67.78 yuan. After the open, the Central Bank announced its official rates, with the British pound stable and the American dollar up by .1875. Customs Gold Units suddenly fell by 0.02, and the standard speculation price dropped to 906.3 yuan. The market opened weakly but quickly regained momentum, briefly surpassing the 70 yuan mark before banks sold to take profits, temporarily halting the rise. News circulated that HSBC's official rates would show a decrease in the British pound by .125, while the American dollar would be little changed, having minimal impact. The market remained mediocre, with many deals occurring after declines. Later, Jardine Matheson attempted to sell but failed, prompting the Central Bank to sell shillings, creating a loose and uncertain atmosphere. This led to wavering long positions and a break below the 60 yuan mark. Sassoon covered short positions at low prices, and large buyers gradually pushed the price back above 60 yuan. Chinese merchants showed increasing interest, fueled by rumors that the Central Bank would repurchase futures contracts at par, boosting confidence. Buying activity then intensified, with prices fluctuating and rising, almost reaching the 70 yuan mark before the Central Bank resumed selling shillings, prompting profit-taking and a midday decline. Swap rates continued to rise, with the long side offering 2.5 yuan. Trading volume was scattered. The following is a record of the market for half the day.

New York Stock Market Rebounds Under the Dominance of Currency Issues 229

Xin Feng Foreign Firm reported that yesterday (the 15th), the New York stock market rebounded, with the largest rebound reaching nearly 2 yuan. Due to the chaotic currency situation in gold standard countries, gold and silver stocks were in high demand and had the strongest prices. The market was entirely dominated by currency issues. The French franc was near the gold export point, the opposite of the recent situation. European speculators sold currencies of gold standard countries and bought British pounds, causing the British pound to rise by three points. The forward selling price of the Belgian currency fell by one point and had no buyers. Foreign exchange experts doubted whether Belgium could maintain its gold standard in the long term. Railway stocks strengthened, as it was widely expected that the Interstate Commerce Commission would soon approve the increase in railway transportation prices. The bond market was mixed and slightly weak. The small exchange rose slightly with mixed results. Wheat rose due to short covering and reports of large dust storms in the southwest. The total daily trading volume was 770,000 shares. The Dow Jones indices are listed on the left.

American Cotton Fluctuates Unpredictably — Reasons for Instability — Another Drop of Over Ten Pounds 233

Yesterday, the state of American cotton, due to political, agricultural, and international monetary conditions, left those in the industry at a loss. At the same time, news from Liverpool was unfavorable. Large quantities were sold off from Liverpool, the mainland, and the Far East. Textile mills engaged in hedging sales to protect unsold textiles, while merchants dumped to protect their unsold spot cotton. This led to an opening drop of 17 to 25 pounds. Later, some industry members, brokers, and local buyers stepped in, and short positions were covered, leading to a slight rebound. However, sentiment remained unstable. Demand is currently poor, but there are not many sellers, and the ground is still firm. Transactions in cotton textiles are slightly better. Hays estimates factory use this week at 276,000 bales, and Liverpool stocks at 309,000 bales. The closing was stable, with no change in spot prices and a drop of 13 to 19 pounds in futures prices. Spot prices for British cotton fell by 10 points, and futures prices fell by 13 to 19 points. Indian cotton was weak due to profit-taking by bulls and a lack of buyers. Agriculture Minister Wallace seems to be too early, and the purchasing power of Southern farmers may not yet be weakened. Market sentiment is mixed, and as soon as there is a turnaround, it encounters profit-taking by bulls.

Food　Stable and Firm Conditions in the Flour and Wheat Market 235

After the flour market opened in the morning, prices for all months generally remained firm. Imported wheat was quoted at 8 to 34 cents higher for Chicago, and 8 to 48 cents higher for Canadian. When the market opened, transactions for all months were not　　robust. Because spot flour is still tight, factories have no inventory, and 1134 flour cannot be exported unless approved daily. Under these circumstances, the market does not seem to be able to fall too much. However, as imported wheat continues to arrive and orders are only shifting in terms of exchange rates, buyers are also difficult to excite. In this environment, the market is mutually rejecting, and transactions are even more sluggish. When the market opened in the afternoon, because factories were not dumping, sentiment stabilized, and coupled with good quotations for imported wheat, market sentiment showed a slight boost. The total transactions for the morning and afternoon factories were only 120,000, which shows the general downturn in the market. As a result, this month was up by half a cent, April and May were up by 7.5 mils, June was up by 1.25 cents, July was up by 7.5 mils, and August was up by 1.25 cents.

After the wheat market opened in the morning and afternoon, prices for all months generally showed a sluggish and stable picture. Imported wheat was quoted at 8 to 34 cents higher for Chicago, and 8 to 48 cents higher for Canadian. When the market opened, because the quotation for imported wheat was slightly better, sentiment naturally showed a slight boost. However, both buyers and sellers were mostly watching and waiting, and transactions were light. In this situation, it will only be lively when new wheat is negotiated. As a result, this month was up by 2 cents, July was up by 2 cents, and August was up by 1 cent. Spot wheat market conditions are quite smooth, but prices have suddenly dropped by 6 to 7 cents, because imported wheat has arrived smoothly, and there is a feeling that there is nothing special to hold on to. Kaishan Dong Guitai wheat was 3 yuan 6 jiao 7 fen, Bengbu Linhuai wheat was 3 yuan 6 jiao half, Xinpu wheat was 3 yuan 6 jiao 35 fen, and Yaowan wheat was 3 yuan 6 jiao, totaling 3,500 bales, handled by Xinda.

(Hu Nan) Yesterday, more than 50 Ke Bang merchants arrived, (nearly 10,000 piculs in total). In this unfavorable weather, people were in a daze, which caused the sales market to be surprisingly sluggish and extremely dull. Although the sellers shouted for lower prices, there were few inquiries. As a result, actual transactions were not many. For example, only Jinan Bang went for two to three hundred bags of each late rice, and the price fell by one or two jiao, while each thick japonica rice dropped two jiao by mistake. Since the Shejian rice has been out of stock for a long time, the market color is fresh in the air, and the Yin Yuan wheat is weak.

Women's World

From Ruan Lingyu to Liu Heying 238

— Wen

The suicide of the actress Ruan Lingyu shocked the minds of people in Shanghai and even the whole country, and earned the tears of many young men and women. This is because her acting skills on the screen made every audience who saw her works admire her wholeheartedly. Her various postures of playing anything like anything were deeply imprinted in the hearts of every audience, making them unable to forget. However, such a talented artist, a movie star loved by millions of viewers, was ultimately buried by the evil society. Ruan Lingyu can only recognize art, but cannot see the society clearly. She cannot use art to expose all the suffering she has suffered and the sins of society to every audience before her death. This is her miscalculation and her weakness. But Ruan Lingyu's suicide is great. Her loyalty to art, her efforts to improve, and her uncompromising work ethic are worthy of admiration by young men and women. Her acting skills are indeed genius, but genius without acquired effort and cultivation, hard work and struggle will still be reduced to mediocrity. Not only will it be reduced to mediocrity, it may even degenerate and be unable to extricate itself. The amazing art Ruan Lingyu left on the screen is definitely not entirely innate. Half is due to her life of painful experiences, and half is due to her dedication and effort to art. Therefore, she is definitely not a decadent woman who uses being a star as a cover, living one day at a time, and taking pleasure as her destination.

When Southern newspapers were filled with news of the death of artist Ruan Lingyu, Northern newspapers were scrambling to publish news of the female writer Liu Heying becoming a prostitute: "Liu Heying, 19 years old, once studied at Beiman Girls' Middle School, and loved literature and art. Three years ago, she had written articles for various small newspapers, and her writing style was fluent and beautiful. Later, she served as a literary editor for a small newspaper and had an affair with a colleague. She was driven out by her father and wandered around. Now she is addicted to opium and has become a third-class prostitute." From this news, we can see that what caused Liu Heying to degenerate was also this evil society and feudal forces. Feudal forces caused a promising young woman to fall into prostitution and sell her body for a living. However, Liu Heying's addiction to opium and no longer striving to write makes her seem to be giving in to self-degradation. Compared with Ruan Lingyu's hard work in art, her half-life of struggle, and her suicide because she could not win, there is a world of difference. However, we still hope that someone will rescue her from the pit of fire, and even more hope that she will use her fluent writing to describe the sins of society and the suffering she has suffered.

The current society is evil, and feudal ethics are eating people everywhere. Young women should strive to understand society, determine their own lives, and take responsibility for transforming this evil society and eliminating feudal forces. This is the right way out. Suicide is not a way out, and depravity is even less of a strategy that young women should take. The real way out is waiting for young women who can endure hardship, be hardworking, and be brave enough to move forward to pave the way.

Women's Issues Lecture

Lecture 3 Women in Prehistoric Times Section 1 The Origin and Evolution of Humanity 239

— Jun Hui

I remember a few years ago, the so-called Monkey Trial happened in the United States, causing a stir. This so-called Monkey Trial was about a professor who "didn't know the times" teaching Darwin's theory of evolution in a certain school, saying that the ancestors of human beings were monkeys, not Adam and Eve from some island. This blasphemous remark actually aroused the anger of the American bourgeoisie and was punished. This thought-provoking case raises the following questions for us.

"Is the Christian Bible right after all? Or is Darwin's theory of evolution right?"

In fact, this problem was solved decades ago. The smart American bourgeoisie also understands the truth of evolution very well. Then why oppose this truth? The reason is very simple, in their eyes there is the consideration of advantages and disadvantages, and there is no such thing as truth or untruth. The Bible is their tool of control. Blaspheming it means blaspheming their right to control!

Since the flourishing of biology and historical science in the 19th century, we have learned that humans were originally a type of animal in the ape family, and evolved into modern humans through the laws of evolution. At the same time, we have learned about the evolutionary process of human society before history. The greatest contributors to this area are Darwin, a biologist, followed by Bachofen, McLennan, Morgan, and Engels, who discovered primitive societies.

What are the ancestors of human beings? Darwin's answer to this question was indeed a rebellious statement in the 19th century, when Christianity ruled Europe and America. According to his research, humans were originally an animal, and like other apes, they foraged for fruits in the woods to fill their stomachs, or hunted small animals to feed themselves. They accidentally picked up stone flakes or wooden sticks and used them as tools for collecting food. From then on, humans occupied a dominant position over other animals. Over thousands of years, due to the practical use of labor tools, the front half of human limbs became particularly specialized, and they ceased to be used for walking, becoming the organs of human labor and defense. At the same time, due to the changes in the function of the hands, humans began to walk upright, and human bones also became straight. Later, due to the practical use and manufacturing of tools; the social nature of labor; upright walking and carnivorism, etc., the physical appearance of human beings completely changed, and they evolved into modern humans. In this way, in the process of evolution from animals to humans, the most decisive basic driving force is the manufacture and use of labor tools. Therefore, the 18th-century American politician Franklin said: "Humans are tool-making animals."

That the ancestors of human beings were animals is not denied by those who understand science, except for those who deliberately抹煞the truth because of class interests.

Secondly, regarding the research of primitive society, the first person to establish a scientific foundation was Morgan. Although before him, there had been Bachofen's discovery of matrilineal society and McLennan's research on the marriage system of primitive humans, it was not until Morgan unified it into a system. He investigated the American Indian nation in the Americas for decades. He detailedly investigated the evolutionary process of primitive society from the formation of "groups", "families", and even "countries", especially his invention of the matrilineal system and the relationship between the sexes in primitive society, which caused a great change in the traditional religious ideas on the issue of gender.

In ancient society, Morgan divided the entire evolutionary process of humans into a savage uncivilized, civilized era, and divided the previous era into early, middle and late three periods, and gave detailed explanations on the human life status of each period. Here, briefly explain its content:

1. Savage Era—Early stage, humans lived in a certain area, using grass roots and tree fruits as food, but already had simple languages; middle stage, began to use fire and used fish as food; later stage, invented bows and arrows, and used birds and animals as food.

2. Uncivilized Era Early stage, invented pottery; middle stage, began to raise animals, cultivate grains, and use dried bricks and stone materials; later stage, invented cast iron and simple writing.

3. Civilized Era—Began to use phonetic alphabets. The written record was made, and the historical era began from then on.

The so-called prehistoric era is the barbaric and uncivilized era. Regarding the issue of the combination of the sexes in this era, Morgan divided it into (1) the blood clan group marriage system, (2) the half-blood clan group marriage system, (3) the pair marriage system, and (4) the polygamy system, which are adapted to the above-mentioned stages.

Each of the above-mentioned eras has new characteristics, which are caused by the changes in human production methods. We believe that the level of development of production methods is the yardstick for dissecting the evolutionary process of human society. Morgan's view coincided very coincidentally with the basic law of historical materialism.

Engels followed Morgan and wrote the book The Origin of the Family, Private Property and the State, and clearly sorted out and explained all of Morgan's research. From then on, the human social situation in the prehistoric era, which had always been hidden in the stuffy gourd, was seen through by people. At the same time, we understood that the religious explanations of the gender issue and the family system were absurd and nonsensical ghost stories!

Finally, let us borrow a passage from Bebel to conclude this section.

"A brief description of the relationship between the sexes in the primitive era is very important for the purpose of this book. This is because we want to prove the following facts and reasons from this. That is, in the process of human evolution in ancient times, the relationship between the sexes has been affected by the changes in production methods and the distribution methods of products. Therefore, in the future, the changes in production and distribution methods will inevitably change the relationship between the sexes. No matter what, there is no "permanently unchanged". In nature and life, the only thing that is permanently unchanged is "transformation" and a change itself." (Women and Society)

Correction 240

In the previous issue of this lecture, "From Female Superiority to Male Superiority," the printing was upside down. We hereby correct it as follows:

The seventh line of the second batch of the previous lecture, "We often hear...even with seven small husbands," should be placed in front of the first line of the first batch.

How to Be a Stepmother 241

— Huan Ying

We know that there are many great figures in history who were only nurtured by the love of their virtuous mothers—they had no fathers since childhood—we can also imagine how, from ancient times to the present, many poor families have been able to prevent their children from dying from cold and hunger. Conversely, we can imagine how unfortunate children without mothers must be!

The relationship between parents and children is natural, unique, and irreplaceable. Why is there such a thing as a stepmother? This is because the organization of current society is not yet perfect, and the responsibility of raising children is still entirely borne by their parents. A father whose child has died of the mother has to marry another woman to be the child's mother—of course, also for his own needs.

Living together is really not an easy thing. Except for loving couples and biological children, even if there are, they are reluctantly formed, not combinations of love. These reluctantly formed groups are bound to have discord—such as jealousy, suspicion, hatred, and all kinds of immoral behaviors, especially in the current economic organization of the family; so I often say "It is difficult to be a stepmother, and it is not easy to be a stepchild!"

Chinese women have been influenced by feudal ideas for thousands of years, and even now few of them have a social concept. Most of them regard children as private property. In addition to the natural love between parents and children, they also harbor the mentality of wanting rewards for raising their own children. As for raising stepchildren, the former factors are lacking and the latter is afraid of being unreliable; so they simply use cruel methods to abuse stepchildren! Facts tell us that before women's knowledge was developed, some of the stepmothers dared not completely abuse stepchildren because they had religious ideas. As for the current group of women in the transitional era, they do not believe in karma, and they do not have a correct understanding of how to be a person. Therefore, these means of abusing stepchildren have become more and more sharp!

As for the psychology of children, it is inevitable that they will develop a distrustful attitude towards their current stepmother because they have heard and seen the scenes of stepmothers abusing stepchildren. Sometimes he will restrain the flow of his innocence, and even he will be ashamed to recognize this hypocritical parent-child relationship.

Under the existing family organization, since stepmothers and stepchildren are so incompatible, how should we remove the barriers between the two?

The solution to the whole problem, of course, is to expect the improvement of social organization, so that women and children become social people. Women not only take on family affairs, but also join society to do productive work, and children are handed over to specialized institutions set up by the state to raise them. In this way, stepmothers will definitely be very polite and harmonious with stepchildren, and will never see them as a thorn in their side as before; but this beautiful future will not be achieved overnight, just like it is difficult to put out a fire far away!

For the sake of unfortunate children, we can only beg the existing or soon-to-be stepmothers: hoping that they will completely change their inherent prejudices, recognize that they are members of society, and can fulfill their duties to society anytime and anywhere. Stepchildren are socially helpless and vulnerable lives. In addition to their fathers, society has clearly designated your responsibility—to represent their mothers—you should especially take responsibility, and raise stepchildren as if they were your own children. If a stepmother treats stepchildren with the determination of utmost fairness and selflessness, I think even if the stepchildren are incompetent and ungrateful, they will be moved and regard her as their own mother.

Being a stepmother is like being a doctor and a nurse, it requires great love. A responsible stepmother is worthy of admiration!

Another Farewell to the Renowned Artist Ruan Lingyu 242

— Sun Shiyi

A line or two of heart-wrenching headlines in the newspaper, thousands of years of built-up potential in the heart. External destruction and internal explosion, she was then martyred by the so-called terrifying human words, and abandoned her great artistic career, leaving her mother and orphans behind and taking a dead end.

On the revolutionary day of the World's March 8th, hundreds of millions of moviegoers in the country, simultaneously and in different places, should remember that this is indeed an immoral society, and must awaken the vast masses of women, and join hands to create a path of life.

Beiping Headhunter Shops 243

— Zi Gang

In China, in every city, female domestic workers constitute a considerable portion of the population. While some women come from the countryside, many seek work in factories. However, with limited opportunities, they must find alternative paths.

In Beiping, factories are not as numerous as in Shanghai or Tianjin. Coupled with the decline of rural areas in recent years, there is an even greater number of female domestic workers. It is common to see wooden signs on the streets and in alleys that read "Female Domestic Worker Placement Agency," along with a note indicating approval from the "Social Affairs Bureau." The owner of the agency is not a man, but a Madam so-and-so.

A few days ago, I accompanied a neighbor to an agency to hire someone. It was a relatively large establishment. A red cloth banner hung on the wooden sign.

We entered a narrow, cramped alleyway. Inside was a rectangular courtyard. Four or five women dressed in dark and light blue clothing stood there in the warm spring sunlight. Some were washing clothes, others were attaching shoe soles.

"Do you have anyone available to send?" the neighbor asked.

An old woman, around sixty years of age, greeted us with a smile. Although thin, she appeared shrewd. Her eyes, set deep in their sockets, scrutinized people. When she smiled, a row of yellowed, mottled teeth were revealed.

"Yes, plenty," she replied, sizing up the person who had spoken. Then she inquired about the number of people in the household and the type of work required. Most importantly, she asked about the wages. Satisfied with the neighbor's response, she pursed her lips.

"Go inside and choose. There are plenty of young and efficient ones."

We entered the main room, which consisted of three sections. One section was partitioned off into an attached room. Five or six men and women sat around a small platform, playing cards. The men were likely family members of the owner or relatives accompanying the domestic workers. The women may have been prospective domestic workers who were still unemployed.

The card players were engrossed in their game, only glancing at us as we stood watching. We returned to the two connected rooms facing outward.

Half of each room was occupied by a large platform bed. A smaller section of the other room also had a wide, raised platform. The platforms were filled with female domestic workers, anxiously waiting for a place to earn a living. There were gaunt, taciturn women who had just arrived from the countryside, gray-haired, elderly women, and seasoned, worldly women transferring from other jobs in the city. Two women with children sat on the platform. The children were suckling at their mothers' breasts, unaware that they may not enjoy the comfort of their mother's milk for much longer.

"Those two are wet nurses," the old owner said. She probably intended to finalize the arrangements before sending the children back to the countryside with someone to care for them. With readily available milk, she was unwilling to spend money on a wet nurse for a few more days. Moreover, the mothers and children were reluctant to part ways so abruptly.

The eighteen or nineteen women on the large platform sat cross-legged, chatting and doing needlework to relieve boredom. Some hoped to sew a new pair of shoes or a new cloth jacket to improve their appearance. Others, resigned, lay down to sleep. Each had her own bedding (unlike in Jiangnan families where the master provides bedding). At night, they would spread out haphazardly, paying four to six copper coins per night for lodging. During the day, they would buy cheap food to fill their stomachs.

"Are there any with large feet?" my neighbor asked, looking around.

The owner laughed. "No, it so happens that all who've come recently have small feet."

A domestic worker, nearly fifty years old, who was washing her feet, chimed in. She was placing a pair of lotus-shaped bound feet in a green basin. "Small feet are no different from large feet, are they? Don't underestimate them. They do a lot of work. They can cook and mop the floor." She said it with a hint of indignation.

The neighbor finally chose a woman in her twenties. Without the "older unmarried daughters" of the South, even a twenty-year-old woman would already be married. It was said that their families were unwilling to let them go, perhaps because they were less progressive.

The owner continued to bargain for a higher wage for the domestic worker. If successful, she would take thirty cents from the first yuan, as was customary. If the wage was four yuan, the domestic worker would have to give her one yuan and twenty cents. At festivals, they would also have to give her one or two dimes. They knew she was exploitative, but they had no choice but to go to her. Even finding her was not easy; one needed a referral from a relative or acquaintance. Otherwise, there was no guarantee of a job.

As we left, we saw five or six people still sitting in the side room. One of them approached and asked,

"Aren't you taking me?"

"You have to wait your turn! They asked for someone specifically," the owner replied. As she saw us to the door, she urged repeatedly,

"Don't call anyone else. I'll send someone for sure tomorrow."

"This person is reliable. Don't call another agency. I'll definitely send someone tomorrow morning." She was afraid we would hire from another agency.

There were too many people seeking work, and those who exploited them struggled even more.

From the city to the countryside, and from the countryside to the city, all were vulnerable, suffering from disaster, disease, and poverty. Only a precarious support system sustained them through these hardships. Perhaps those who had recently fled the famine in the countryside would feel a temporary sense of relief. But if they stayed long enough, they would wonder in bewilderment:

"When will the day come when there isn't even a place to sell one's labor?"

Discussion on the Joint Guarantee System for Private Prostitutes 244

— Bo Er

The economic downturn has affected public brothels, making business slow. Unable to afford heavy taxes, they gradually become private prostitutes. Furthermore, rural areas across the country are facing bankruptcy, and factories in urban areas are experiencing reduced sales, leading to an increase in unemployed female workers. Unable to sustain themselves, many are forced to engage in secret prostitution. Recent surveys in Guangzhou estimate that there are over 20,000 private prostitutes.

The difference between public and private prostitutes lies in whether they possess a government-issued business license. Those who engage in private prostitution do so to avoid the burden of taxes and levies. However, authorities believe that the proliferation of private prostitution is detrimental to public morals, and they have issued strict orders to investigate, arrest, and punish offenders. Fines typically range from three to several tens of yuan each time.

When these women secretly leave the brothel to entertain or spend the night with clients, they are required to split the meager earnings of three to several yuan with the waiters in the brothel, with the introducer taking 40% and the women retaining only 60%. Out of the 60% they receive, they must also pay for rent, electricity, servants, and food. Having sold their bodies, the money they earn is shared with others. In the end, what remains for themselves amounts to only a few dimes, which is barely enough to cover their expenses for clothing and treatment for venereal diseases.

Therefore, they exhaust every possible means to disguise themselves as female students, loitering in crowded places, employing all sorts of flirtatious tactics to lure men to their secret lairs. Some are sold into servitude and subjected to harsh treatment by their madams, leaving them unable to solicit clients freely or afford the fines imposed upon being caught. As a means of coping with the struggles of survival, they devised a way to share their burden: the "joint guarantee system." They would form groups of ten or more, and if one of them was caught, they would pool their money to pay the fine on her behalf.

This leads us to a question: can we truly eliminate or reduce the proliferation and negative impact of prostitution, uphold morality, and guide women onto the right path through coercive measures such as levying taxes? In reality, the life of a prostitute is far from easy. Which prostitute doesn't yearn for a life of happiness, just like everyone else? Who doesn't want to secure a legitimate occupation in society? Sadly, these are women who have been excluded and abandoned by every sector of society (some also possess limited knowledge), leaving them with no other options. Are they not also essentially good people forced down a path by society, just like everyone else? Now that they have fallen from public to private prostitution, they struggle to sustain themselves even in the secret lives of private prostitutes, leading them to establish the joint guarantee system… in order to preserve and prolong their lives. Such an infinitely variable approach to preserving a life that is barely human. Can this be stopped by any kind of pressure? Can it be eradicated by a mere formal campaign to abolish prostitution?

British Women's Anti-War Movement 245

London Dispatch: During a heated debate in Parliament on a Labour Party motion to impeach the government for its military expansion policy, an unexpected interruption occurred. Several women in the audience threw leaflets advocating peace, scattering paper throughout the assembly hall. These women also loudly condemned the government's defense white paper. They were immediately escorted out by parliamentary police. Subsequently, several other women in the audience staged a similar demonstration and were also expelled. Simultaneously, a crowd of approximately two hundred people, mostly women, gathered outside the Parliament building, intending to meet with lawmakers to express their opposition to the government's policies.

A Visit to "Glutinous Rice Ball Beauty" 246

— Lu Er Yu

Although the cry for gender equality has long been resounding, it is not easy to determine to what extent women's rights have actually been extended in the past decade or two. Recently, our local newspapers have been vigorously promoting beauty contests, with "Glutinous Rice Ball Beauty," "Blacksmith Beauty," and "Lipstick Beauty" all being considered for selection. Is electing "beauties" elevating women's rights? In any case, I believe it contains an element of insult. Men's tricks for making fun of women are becoming increasingly innovative, and women cannot tolerate this kind of disguised insult! However, the "beauty group" in our county accepts it submissively and even "smiles with delight," which is truly perplexing! To understand the "beauty group's" submissiveness, I took action to visit the "Glutinous Rice Ball Beauty" on the afternoon of February 11th!

A small, two-dish restaurant-like glutinous rice ball shop at the entrance of North Gate Lane was doing thriving business. The two tables were full, leaving no room to squeeze in. The customers, who appeared to be students, were joking and laughing casually. The so-called "Glutinous Rice Ball Beauty" had a fair, oval face, disheveled hair, and a tall figure. She dealt with the customers very skillfully, always smiling. Young men flocked to the shop, coming to have a cigarette and a couple of glutinous rice balls, which was much more economical than going to a teahouse! Such is the psychology of men and women! It was difficult to find a spot in the corner of the shop, giving me only five minutes for the interview.

I began my visit to the "beauty":

"Are you called Beauty, is that right! I've heard so much about you!"

"It's all nonsense. The newspaper folks are making up some 'beauty' for me. I don't understand it, sir!" She giggled for a while.

"You seem very happy! I know!"

Her face suddenly tightened, and she said softly, "You know!"

"Business is good, isn't it!"

"Business isn't bad. I make about ten or more yuan a day!"

"Good business should make you happy. No one can keep up with you!"

"Good business makes me happy? Hmm!"

"I walk past your shop every day, and you always seem to be smiling and greeting customers!"

"What else can I do? If I don't, how will I eat? Do I want to do this?"

A small handkerchief lightly covered her eyes.

The shop assistants in the glutinous rice ball shop glared at me. I knew that I had stirred up trouble with my words. Then, the door slammed open, and two young men with dark hair and in Western suits rushed in. The "beauty's" hand was squeezed tightly. She greeted them with a smile.

"Have a seat! Mr. Pan!"

"Four ounces of Chen Shao wine, four glutinous rice balls, and sixty cash worth of peanuts."

I walked out of the shop.

Along the way, I thought about how there are many women similar to the "Glutinous Rice Ball Beauty" among the 200 million female compatriots. For the sake of livelihood, they are tossed about under the lash of suffering. While the women's rights movement has been fought very vigorously, the result has only been the liberation of women in the upper and middle classes. The "Glutinous Rice Ball Beauty" will never be liberated in her lifetime!

The Courtesan's Demands 247

— Wu Yue

Recently, while leafing through old newspapers I had previously clipped, I felt that many old stories were worth revisiting. Here is one small item among the many old stories that is worth mentioning. I will now transcribe it below:

"After being abandoned by a former Qing dynasty official with a purple ribbon, a high-ranking courtesan entered a women's reformatory to find a suitable match. There was no shortage of people hoping to marry her. However, because two of the courtesan's demands could not be met, she refused to compromise. The two demands are: (1) The man must be of a suitable age, and she refuses to be a concubine. (2) The good man who marries her must respect her right to freedom and must not infringe upon it in any way. Upon hearing these demands, all those who wished to marry her found them to be difficult to fulfill, it is said."

After reading these two demands of the courtesan, I felt that they were very ordinary conditions. Why did those who wished to marry her find them difficult to fulfill? I thought that since there was no shortage of people hoping to marry her, the demand for a "suitable age" would probably not be a problem. The problem clearly lay in the issues of being a concubine versus a wife and the need to respect her freedom and not infringe upon it in any way.

Upon careful consideration, these two conditions are mutually contradictory. A man who cannot afford to take a concubine would certainly respect her freedom and would not infringe upon it, but such a man would not be able to support her. A man who can afford to spend money on her, even if he does not take her as a concubine, would at least not respect her freedom and would always infringe upon it to some extent. Therefore, in the end, everyone felt that these two conditions were difficult!

In fact, the courtesan's situation reflects the fate of women in general. When women follow poor men, they always argue because he cannot support her. When women follow rich men, they always complain because he mistreats her.

The fundamental cause of this situation naturally goes back to the economic relations of the society at the time. Women's inability to be independent and their dependence on men are entirely characteristic of our society.

This old news item is already about ten years old. Now, women already have occupations. However, if we were to republish this old news item in the newspaper, people would certainly believe that it was a recently occurring news story, wouldn't they? This illustrates that these two very ordinary conditions that the courtesan demanded are still considered difficult to fulfill even after ten years!

Alas, after so many years of women's movements, even the courtesan's demands have not been granted, so what is there to talk about in terms of women's liberation! If things continue in this way, I believe that the courtesan's demands will never be granted if the economic relations of society do not change.

The Shanghai News Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

"Hard" and "Soft" Articles 248

— Lie

I say, there are two types of writing: "hard" and "soft." By "hard" articles, I mean theoretical articles on science, politics, economics, and so on. By "soft" articles, I mean poems, novels, plays, lifestyle sketches, humorous pieces, essays, and the like – articles with artistic characteristics. If all articles express human thoughts and feelings, then the characteristic of "hard" articles is that they discuss theories, using the power of understanding to express certain thoughts and feelings. "Soft" articles are the opposite; their characteristic is not in discussion but in description, vividly and concretely depicting certain thoughts and feelings. Good "hard" articles explain a truth in detail from all aspects. Those who are good at writing such articles not only have correct views but also possess very rich arguments. They do not engage in abstract concepts or list formulas casually, but explain a correct theory with many practical and historical examples. They not only have abundant materials but also possess a systematic scientific method. They can gradually and methodically integrate their materials into their theory, without any confusion. When they write, it's like peeling bamboo shoots, layer by layer, very clearly, without any omissions or mixtures, making it very easy for the reader to understand. Therefore, although good "hard" articles are relatively rigid, they are also interesting to read. For example, the "hard" articles of Engels and Plekhanov, although their theories are very profound and not easy to understand without a higher level of philosophical and scientific knowledge, if you have the ability to read their works, you will find that everything they say is logical, and they capture your heart with undeniable facts and truths. As for those shallow and foolish people who write "hard" articles, they either pile up materials in a chaotic manner or play with abstract nouns or overuse formulas. Therefore, regardless of whether the theory itself is correct, their articles become increasingly annoying to read. Like the good "hard" articles mentioned above, good "soft" articles depict human life very subtly and concretely from all aspects. Those who are good at writing "soft" articles have a deep understanding of the life they want to depict. The scenes they create are completely alive, making the reader feel as if they are present in the scene. The emotions of joy, anger, sadness, and fear that they express are extremely real, immediately evoking the same emotions in the reader. When we read Dostoevsky's "Crime and Punishment," when our eyes encounter the protagonist's murder and the situation after the murder, our hearts also beat faster, feeling a little afraid, but no matter how afraid we are, we still want to read on enthusiastically. Similarly, when we read Bernard Shaw's humorous articles, we also laugh. When we see the most tragic scene in Tolstoy's "Resurrection," we can't help but shed tears, feeling great sadness. What is the reason for this? I believe it is because those great writers are good at writing "soft" articles. They can truly and artistically express a certain form of human life, thought, and emotion, making you unable to avoid feeling deeply moved when you read them.

Although "hard" and "soft" articles each have their own characteristics, they are not absolutely different. In my opinion, there is "softness" in "hard" articles, and there is "hardness" in "soft" articles. "Hard" articles are not as hard as steel, without any gentleness. "Soft" articles are not as soft as cotton, without any strength. Obviously, good "hard" articles can not only conquer people's thoughts but also move people's feelings. Those who are good at writing "hard" articles naturally have very correct thoughts and very passionate feelings. When they write, they not only avoid dry and tasteless discussions but also use vivid words to describe the thoughts they express. Therefore, I say there is "softness" in "hardness." Similarly, good "soft" articles are also written under the guidance of correct theories. Someone who is good at writing "soft" articles not only possesses great artistic expression but also has a progressive worldview. When they express a certain social life, they are not doing so unconsciously but consciously depicting it under the guidance of their progressive worldview. Therefore, I also say there is "hardness" in "softness."

However, because "soft" articles have more emotional content and depict social life vividly and figuratively, using words that we use in daily life, they are easy to read and understand without much thought. Some people who write "hard" articles often like to use the form of "soft" articles to express their "hard" theories, and that is because of the aforementioned. At present, the general cultural level in China is certainly very low, and more advanced "hard" theories are not easily understood by novice readers. Therefore, some people who write "hard" articles often look for problems in the daily lives of general readers, using the form of "soft" articles (such as plays, novels, or storytelling) to express their "hard" theories. For example, the "Street Talks" in "New Life" and the various academic lectures in the new magazines that "softly" write "hard" articles can all be said to have arisen from this. This method of "softly" writing "hard" articles is certainly very good, but it is not easy to write such articles well because it requires not only correct theories and a deep understanding of the lives of general readers but also considerable descriptive talent. However, it is difficult for those who are used to writing "hard" articles to immediately acquire all these knowledge and abilities and "soften" their articles appropriately. Therefore, I advise those who write "hard" articles that if they have the talent to "soften" their "hard" articles, they can certainly do so to increase their impact on society. If they do not have this talent, then I hope they will learn slowly and not rush to publish those inferior "hard" articles written in a soft manner, lest they disturb the eyes of the general readers. Truly, those who do not have the talent to "soften" "hard" articles, if they insist on forcing themselves to do so, the result will certainly be something that is neither "hard" nor "soft," and it will be like nothing at all. Recently, I have seen many articles that use the form of "soft" articles to talk about the "hard" theories of natural science, and they not only lack the fun of "soft" articles but also make the content empty because the authors are desperately trying to work on the form (and the form is certainly not well-worked), ultimately making their articles neither male nor female, like nothing at all. I believe that such articles that "softly" write "hard" articles are no better than good original "hard" articles. Therefore, I say: do what you can do, and don't do things you can't do and make a fool of yourself!

Life

Page 20

and various academic lectures in new magazines that "soft write" hard articles etc, they can be said to be born out of this. Of course this method of "soft writing" hard articles is good, but it is not easy to write this type of article, because this not only needs to have correct theories, also needs to have profound understanding about the life of general readers, and also needs to have significant descriptive talent, but it is difficult for people who are used to "hard writing" hard articles to immediately fully have these knowledge and abilities, and to "soften" their articles reasonably, so I advise to general people who "hard write" hard articles, if they have "soft" talent, then it is of course acceptable to "soft write" their hard articles, to increase its effect on society, if they do not have this type of talent, then it is hoped that they will slowly go to learn, do not rush to then publish the low-level hard article written in a soft manner, and go to disturb the eyes of general readers. Truly, if those who do not have the talent to "soft write" hard articles, if they must "hard" their scalp to "soft" dry, then what they write will certainly be "hard" is not "hard", "soft" is not "soft", doesn't look like anything. Regarding this I say: can do what, still go do what, don't go do what you can't do and embarrass yourself!

Railway Heroes 249

— Chen Shuxun

All those who seek to profit on the Pinghan Railway – vagrants, hooligans, disbanded soldiers – are called "Wild Cavalry Braves." This is a nickname given to them by railway personnel, and its history is perhaps as old as the railway itself.

These fellows are perhaps the sons of farmers, or brothers of workers; in short, they have no land and no work. For the sake of survival, they have learned the tricks of petty theft. And because the railway provides them with opportunities to steal, they come here to seek profit.

Obviously, they are neither employees nor passengers, but they are constantly moving in and out of the carriages, running around the stations. What are they doing running around? Naturally, they are trafficking in smuggled goods, stealing luggage, stealing coal, and deceiving villagers. In short, they are engaging in all sorts of irregular tricks!

Northern heroin (white powder) relies on them to be transported to Hankou, and southern opium relies on them to be transported to Beijing. They are the saviors of addicts and the salesmen of human sin (others create the sin). But they do not understand the harm or benefit to society; they only know that if they can obtain profit, they will do anything!

The so-called smuggled goods are not just drugs; they include all business that can make money and evade customs duties. For example, pears and dates from Cizhou (between Henan and Hebei provinces, where Cao Cao's seventy-two tombs are located) can be sold to Hankou for double the profit, and bringing copper coins back to Beijing can yield a 40% profit. There is no empty return trip, and there is plenty of profit to be made.

However, to do this business, one must have at least: first, capital; second, reputation. What business can you do without capital? Who would dare to risk transporting smuggled goods without the ability to operate? Ordinary vagrants and hooligans do not dare and cannot do this, so those who engage in this business usually have other backgrounds, or are directly managed by the old heroes among the Wild Cavalry Braves. As for poor fellows just starting out, they each find a way to make a living according to their own abilities. The younger ones have to steal coal. But although they are small, their skills are extraordinary. When the coal car is two or three li from the station, they leap into the carriage. They lift the coal blocks up and pass them down, and people below move them elsewhere. By the time the car enters Yangqi (about half a li from the station), they have finished their work and slipped across the opposite wasteland. Every coal train that stops at the station loses at least several tons of coal. Although there are police guards along the way, it is difficult to take care of everything. The prerequisite for stealing coal is to learn to grab the train. No matter how fast or slow it is, one must be able to get on and off freely (naturally, there are also those who die in the attempt). Even if the guards try to catch them, they cannot. If they want to shoot, they feel it is too trivial. In fact, coal is their life. Even if a gun or knife is held to their neck, they will still try to reclaim their life. Moreover, their clothing blends with the coal ash, forming a natural camouflage. If it is a hazy night, no one can tell whether they are people or coal!

Those who steal luggage are mostly strong young heroes. Not only are they skilled at grabbing trains, but they are also capable of all kinds of stealing techniques, because they practice this skill every day of the year. They can skillfully disguise themselves and blend in with the passengers. If they want to steal from a soldier, they will dress up as an officer themselves. In short, their attire must be changed at any time according to the type of business. What they steal is naturally mostly small things (such as handbags, hats, small suitcases), but sometimes even quilts and large suitcases are stolen. Often, the theft is successful and the owner is unaware. Even if they discover it early, there is nothing they can do, because the thief can jump off the train. This kind of business is usually done by several people together: someone is on the lookout, someone does the stealing, and someone blocks the owner. Everything is arranged very well, and it is rare for things to go wrong. However, it is more difficult in the first-class and second-class carriages of express trains. There are constables and police here, and there are fewer passengers, making it difficult to hide. If it is a slow train, it is very casual. There are no noble passengers here, and no police protection. As long as they take a fancy to something, they can get it nine times out of ten. If you take a slow train from Hankou, the crowd is so dense that you can hardly breathe. Most of them are here to seek profit. Once you pass Hengdian, you will notice that the number of people decreases, but at this time you can hear at least a few people shouting that they have lost something. The first few stations of the train rarely check tickets, so there are particularly many people who want to seek profit. When they arrive at the station, whether they have achieved their purpose or not, they mostly jump off the train and wait for the opposite train to come, so that they can find return business.

There is also a type of disbanded soldier who roams the railways. Because they have their own set of broken military uniforms or old insignia, they can ride slow trains and coal trains very freely. Thus, they often travel on the Pinghan Railway, on the one hand engaging in petty theft, and on the other hand deceiving the common people. The methods of deception are nothing more than: first, posing as recruitment committee members. Three or five people patrol the streets and alleys, waving recruitment flags. When they see a young boy, they boast: that place is prosperous, that unit has good treatment – three meals of rice, a salary of more than ten silver dollars, talking a blue streak, with oily mouths. Thus, they lure apprentices and farmers' sons. After they have registered, they deliberately publicize it to the parents. If the parents do not want their son to be a soldier, they must pay money to redeem him. Otherwise, the soldier's clothes and money will be swindled away by the "recruiters." Second, escorting passengers: villagers always love money and are reluctant to pay for train tickets when they want to go out. The disbanded soldiers hear this news, so they volunteer to take someone there, requiring only a few cents for tea money, and promising to ensure everything. The villagers are greedy for cheapness, and know that the soldier lords have this ability, so they fumble around and produce a few cents, and timidly follow the soldier lords onto the train. But soon the soldier lord slips away and disappears. They have to fumble for money to buy a ticket – or perhaps be kicked off the train.

When we arrive on the north bank of the Yellow River, if we pay attention, we can see recruitment committee members waving paper flags at every major station (Xinxiang, Zhangde, Shunde, Baoding, etc.). These are the disbanded soldiers who deceive the common people. At the same time, every slow train and coal train is filled with gray animals, at least half of whom are Wild Cavalry Braves. Why do these fellows like to operate on the north bank of the Yellow River? According to my guess, perhaps it is because the poor boys in the north envy the rice in the south!

The entire Pinghan Railway has become the territory for the Wild Cavalry Braves to operate. However, because of the different regional environments, various roles have also emerged. The north produces heroin, and there are also particularly many drug dealers. Zhangde produces coal, and the coal-stealing boys can form teams. As for the cutthroats like Li Gui, the area from Hankou to Xinyangzhou is the most prevalent, especially between Guangshui and Wushengguan, which is the place for heroes to display their talents. They not only rob luggage, but sometimes also send you back to your hometown: I have encountered being thrown off the tracks twice in this area. According to people on the same train: the first time was revenge, the second time was because the owner resisted. At the time, I was really wary, and felt that the difficulty of traveling was greater than ascending to the blue sky! These fellows like to cause trouble here, simply because there are more mountains, which are convenient for escape, and not as others say: the people of Hubei are inherently unruly!

The railway heroes, on the surface, naturally display their own unique abilities, with no one to control them. In fact, there is a close organization inside, with each having its own scope of activities. Coal thieves cannot rob luggage. The Wild Cavalry Braves on the north bank of the Yellow River cannot cross the south bank to intercept wealth (there are also times when they collude). Each organization has strict discipline, with the highest leader (the boss). The little fellows charge and fight outside, and all the wealth they obtain is handed over to the boss, who distributes it freely. However, although the boss sits and divides gold and silver, he also has to support the little fellows in ordinary times, and must also take full responsibility if any trouble is caused. The situation is similar to that of the Gelaohui.

The title and position of "boss" are entirely obtained through struggle. In the history of the Wild Cavalry Braves, it is unknown how many meritorious deeds have been recorded. Today, the hooligans and rascals on the Pinghan Railway have a place to live, all thanks to the foundation laid by the bosses. He claims to be alone and leads the masses, which is entirely appropriate. To know that a dignified transportation agency is actually being infiltrated by them, who can say that the boss has no merit, no ability?

If one earns the name "Wild Cavalry Brave," it is equivalent to Zhang Heng and Li Jun on Jieyang Ridge, who can dominate one side. Who would dare to call him a vagrant or a hooligan? Who would dare to call him a bad egg? If he wants to show his power, he can immediately call up hundreds of brothers, and perhaps the transportation agency will be thrown into chaos!

Industry Investigation

Huai Bei Brewing Industry 250

— Shu Xun

The brewing industry in Huaibei is not only the best in Jiangsu Province, but also compares favorably with the wine-producing regions of the entire country!

The main products of the rural areas there are sorghum and wheat, both of which are raw materials for wine. The wineries do not have to obtain them from distant markets. At the same time, many winery owners are mostly landlords who own wheat fields, and use their own raw materials to brew their own wine, which can save a lot of trouble (even if they still need to buy, it is supplied by nearby markets). Moreover, rather than selling sorghum and wheat, it is more profitable to turn them into wine. For these reasons, the brewing industry has become widespread in Huaibei.

If we tour Huaibei for a week, we can find many wineries in the villages and towns of Donghai, Guanyun, Ganyu, Lianshui, and Muyang. In short, the entire Huaibei is a wine-producing area. From this we can know the important relationship between the brewing industry and the rural economy. It can also be said that the winery is the representative of the Huaibei rural economy. From its prosperity or decline, we can measure the real situation of the countryside.

Wineries come in different sizes, and the wine they produce is also divided into two categories (i.e., what the locals call "big wine" and "small wine"). Large wineries brew "sorghum wine" (the name is sorghum wine, but the raw materials are sorghum and wheat mixed together). Small wineries can only produce "local-brewed imitation Shaoxing wine" (small wineries are also called "small pot stills," and local-brewed wine is also called "local yellow wine"). The two not only have different names, but also differ greatly in value and sales. However, I will simply point out: big wine can be sold in distant places, and each dan (100 jin on a scale) costs about 20 yuan or more. Small wine is only retailed locally, and each zuo costs a maximum of 8 yuan. It must also be explained that large wineries are completely commercial organizations, while small wineries are only considered a side business of farmers. Whether they brew wine or close down is not planned.

Compared to other wine-producing regions, Donghai and Ganyu produce more? Muyang's wine tastes the best, so its value is higher both locally and far away (Muyang wine costs 27 or 28 yuan per dan, while others only sell for 22 or 23 yuan). However, that depends on whether the buyer is an expert, because the wine transported to distant places all carries the "Huaibei Wine" brand. The quality of the wine naturally depends on the quality of the water. Wine brewed with water that contains less salt tastes better, otherwise it is the opposite. It should be known that ordinary drinks in Huaibei are salty. It is harder to drink a cup of "fresh water" tea than it is for a poor person to drink coffee!

The main markets for Huaibei wine are Shanghai and Nanjing. At its peak, the wine sold in Shanghai alone averaged around 1,000 dan per month, and the value was also very high. The winery owners were mostly fat and well-fed, and their pockets were also full. This aroused the envy of speculators, and many local tyrants and gentry transformed themselves into wine merchants. At that time, there were more than 80 large wineries in Ganyu County alone. If we count the entire Huaibei, it is a large number.

But good times don't last forever, and the full moon is hard to see again. The prosperous scene has become a memory of the past. Under the shadow of this nationwide economic recession, the brewing industry cannot escape its bad fate: sales are blocked and prices are falling. The wine that used to be sold exclusively in Shanghai has changed its course and is being sold chaotically in nearby counties.
