Biographies

Biography of Einstein (Continued to End) 251

— Cong Mu

In Germany, the "Berliner Illustrirte Zeitung" published a portrait of Einstein in November 1919. The people of Berlin then knew that such a great scholar lived in the same city as them. Later, Einstein's name spread throughout Germany, and some even named their newborn children Albert. For a time, Einstein and his theory of relativity became a fad in the world. However, at the same time, the resentment caused by Einstein being Jewish also rose higher and higher.

In 1921, Einstein was invited to lecture in Paris, which was the first time that France had invited a member of the German intelligentsia after the war. But at that time, the hatred between France and Germany was very deep, and it was dangerous to speak German in the streets of Paris, so the organizers who invited Einstein specifically explained to people that he was Swiss, not German. At that time, Einstein was of course a newcomer in the German academic world, and there were many people who doubted his theories, but after listening to his lecture, everyone admired him. The mathematician and mechanician Painlevé was also one of them.

Not long after, Einstein was invited to lecture in London. When he took the stage to speak, Lord Haldane introduced him to the audience: This man is the Newton of the twentieth century, even greater than Newton, a person who has awakened an intellectual revolution. It is said that because he was a Jewish German, no one initially applauded to welcome him. After Lord Haldane's skilled introduction, the audience noticed the importance of this new discovery and realized that learning and art have no borders. Thus, Einstein was welcomed. After that, he went to lecture and teach in various parts of the United States, and of course he was very popular. It is said that once when he lectured in a certain city, there were as many as five or six thousand people in the audience.

In 1922, Einstein was invited to Japan by the "Kaizosha" and was also very popular.

(Six)

After the outbreak of the war, Einstein had nothing to do with general mobilization because he was a Swiss national. At the same time, he did not participate in the famous declaration issued by ninety-three German university professors during the war. At this time, no matter how tense the surrounding atmosphere was, he still worked hard on his research and completed the general theory of relativity. His attitude was like Hegel's during the Napoleonic Wars. However, the German nationalists during the war were very opposed to the Jews, and after Germany's defeat, this anti-Jewish situation became even more intense. They thought that the revolutions in Russia and Germany at that time, and the unrest in Europe, were all the result of the conspiracy of the Jewish people. Einstein was Jewish, and of course he was an object of opposition. His theory of relativity, which was called a scientific revolution, was also regarded by those anti-Jewish people as one of the Jewish people's conspiracies to subvert the world, and was attacked.

After the war, when the rejection of Jews was at its height in Germany, one day in 1919, Jewish intellectuals in Berlin gathered in a restaurant to discuss the future of the Jewish people. Einstein had originally left the shackles of the Jewish association, but he attended this meeting. After quietly listening to the speeches of those Jewish people, he had the idea of saving the Jewish people from their real suffering. This was not because he himself was Jewish, and completely out of selfish psychology, nor was it due to a momentary emotional impulse, nor was it because he had any Jewish ideas and reasons. No, the reason why he did this was because the Jewish people had suffered cruel abuse, and he was standing on the position of humanitarianism, wanting to rescue them from the abuse. From then on, Einstein contributed his great strength to the Jewish question.

By 1933, the political situation in Germany had changed, and Einstein was greatly coerced by the authorities. He left his residence in Belgium in September of that year and went to England, and in October he crossed the sea to America. He is still continuing his great research, and is using his spare time to lecture in universities in the United States and France. (End)

The old signboards with large capital can still be maintained, otherwise they will lose money and cry out in pain!

So they struggled hard and came up with many tricks to escape the great disaster in front of them. The so-called "tricks" are nothing more than saving expenses (abolishing apprenticeships, laying off workers) and reducing costs: they tried to mix as much local yellow wine as possible into the sorghum wine they transported and sold in distant places. In each zuo, there were at least 70% small wine, but they still used the brand of big wine. In this way, although the market price was low, the cost was reduced. At the same time, they did not wholesale local yellow wine from small wineries. They also set up small pot stills as needed, and their function was naturally to produce local yellow wine, which was specially used to dilute big wine.

But this effect is only equal to sleeping pills. Over time, it is still a policy of suicide. On the one hand, wholesalers can only be cheated once, and at the same time, "the deadline is approaching," and no matter how hard they struggle, it is only a deathbed glow! The recent situation has become even more dangerous: the wine transported to Shanghai has been reduced to 17 or 18 yuan and there are still no customers. Many wineries' "runzhang" (wine salesmen) have been stranded in Shanghai for half a year, and they are just sighing at the inventory! As for the story of the robbers who copy small roads often have the joke of the original jar of wine turning back. The sales in distant places have been blocked, but there are many wines that have never been out of the house, and they are transported to Shanghai and Nanjing during this bad wind, which is not learning fashion, but is really an unavoidable contradiction! It should be known that if the winery does not brew wine, the cellar mouth will deteriorate after a considerable period of time. If the wine is put into a jar, the amount will gradually be lost, and in order to take out the capital, it has to be sold urgently. But the local sales are limited, and the competition between the wineries is fierce. In this way, they have no choice but to transport it to other places to try their luck!

Last year, the entire Huaibei winery almost came to its final fate. About 50 large wineries announced that they were closing down, and as for small pot stills, it can be said that they have all closed down. Among them, Ganyu suffered the greatest losses, because Liu Hei Qi (Liu Guitang)'s bandit army once looted the county seat, and disrupted the countryside for several months (such as Shahe and other places bordering Shandong). During the looting and disturbance, the sales of wine were blocked, and the capital was also extracted, and under the trampling of the cavalry, the wine jars and cellar mouths had to be destroyed!

In short, the brewing industry in Huaibei has declined from prosperity to depression, withering, and desolation! I have seen large wineries reducing the number of cellar mouths (the more cellar mouths, the more prosperous the business is), and I have also seen them dismantling boilers and selling livestock, until they "close their doors and declare victory"!

The decline of the brewing industry is not only the bad luck of the winery owners, but also affects the entire Huaibei countryside! (Naturally, the bankruptcy of the countryside affects the brewing industry.) As mentioned above, the main products of Huaibei are sorghum and wheat, both of which are raw materials for wine. In the era of prosperity of the brewing industry, wineries accounted for two-quarters of the sales of both. Now that many wineries have closed down, sales have decreased by at least 10%. In the past, wheat could also be sold to Shanghai and Nanjing, but it was resisted by American wheat, and not only did the market price fall, but it could not even be exported. (American wheat occupies the quasi-city market!) In this case, the landlords who own wheat fields are also burnt out!

Also: the winery in the villages of Huaibei is like a rural money house. It sells cash back elsewhere, buys local raw materials, and disperses the cash. At least it has the function of regulating finance for the Huaibei countryside. At the same time, the development of the brewing industry means that wineries need more labor, so that some of the unemployed in the countryside have a place to eat. But now that wineries are gradually closing down, the rural economy is extremely poor, and the unemployed group has added many new forces. In this way, the decline of the Huaibei brewing industry has such a serious impact on the countryside!

— Ying

In the face of the current urgent world economic crisis, both Chinese and foreign people are doing their best to explore a way out of recovery or prosperity. The United States is the richest country in the world; at the same time, it is also the main part of the world economic crisis that has deepened the most. Although people may not take the United States as an example when seeking a way to recover or prosper, recalling the historical situation of American capitalism when it dominated the world with a rapid posture in those years may be of some help to our understanding and research!

As early as four or five years ago, when the American economy was prospering, its heavy industry production accounted for about half of the world's total. At that time, its coal mining volume accounted for 45% of the world's total; cast iron, pig iron and steel accounted for 50%; and oil accounted for two-thirds. As for the production volume of copper, tin, zinc, etc., it also ranked first among the countries of the world. The development of light industry can almost be said to have advanced completely in conjunction with the development of heavy industry. Echoes of the Past 253

— Piyi

Guanzi said, "Think and think again, think even harder. If you think but cannot understand, the spirits will enlighten you. This is not the power of spirits, but the utmost sincerity."

Zhang Hongfan was a Yuan general who helped Kublai Khan unify China. When his army reached Yashan in Guangdong, later generations mocked him in a poem: "Zhang Hongfan carved his name on Yashan, not a barbarian, but a Han Chinese."

Lord Fan Zhongyan once said to people: "It's easy to be a regular official, but hard to eat regular meals." Lu Ling Tan Dajing said: "If a man can be content with eating regular meals, then he can be content with being a regular official." This saying is also enlightening.

Xin You'an sent a poem to Qiu Zongqing, saying: "For thousands of years, where can one find Sun Quan, the hero of the Yangtze River? The pavilions and towers, once filled with romance, are now swept away by wind and rain. The setting sun shines on the grass and trees, and ordinary alleys. People say that Liu Yu once lived here. Imagine the iron horses of that year, with a spirit that devoured thousands of miles like a tiger. Yuanjia hastily sealed Langjuxu, only to win a hurried glance north. Forty-three years, looking at the lights in the distance, I still remember the road to Yangzhou. Alas, looking back, beneath the shrine of Emperor Tuoba Tao, there is only a scene of divine crows and community drums. Who can ask if Lian Po is old and can still eat?" This poem is exquisite and magnificent, worthy of immortality.

Layman Dongpo said: "Raising a cat is to catch mice. One should not raise a cat that does not catch mice when there are no mice." Nowadays, there are those who raise cats that do not catch mice, but instead catch chickens. Is it acceptable to raise such a cat?

After Yan Ziling helped Emperor Guangwu restore the Han Dynasty, he drifted away into seclusion, whereabouts unknown. Someone saw him wearing a fur coat, fishing by the riverbank. Emperor Guangwu searched for him, but again, his whereabouts were unknown. People all said that his character was one level above others. However, someone later wrote a poem satirizing him: "Once he put on a sheepskin coat, he had ambitions. His false name has been praised to this day. If he had worn ordinary clothes back then, where could he be found in the vast Yin River?" Is this an excessive criticism?

When Hu Dan'an met Yang Shishan, Guishan raised both elbows to show him and said: "My elbows have not left this desk for thirty years. Only then have I made progress in the Way." Is this what is called studying to death?

In all matters, one should always have a mind like a rolling ball and hands like a sounding arrow. This is what Yang Dongshan said.

Yi Yin served Tang five times and Jie five times, and the people of the world never considered it a disgrace. Su Shi commented on it, saying: "Those who handle great affairs of the world have great integrity; those who establish great integrity for the world are broad-minded. If the greatness of the world is not enough to move their hearts, then great integrity cannot be established, and great affairs cannot be handled."

One man is enough to surpass Yu, and three households can destroy Qin. Facts prove both.

When Li Ji was on his deathbed, he said to his younger brother: "If my sons and younger brothers have ambitions that are inappropriate or associate with the wrong people, kill them first and then report it to me." His words were so stern.

Recently, the Shanghai Cunwen Association and others issued a declaration, saying: "With the fear of Yi Chuan for the Rong people, we pledge to serve the country with our writings." Is this the beginning of the saying "serve the country with writings"? Another way to save the country has been added.

The third day of the third month is the memorial day of the fall of my hometown county. Waking up on this day, I immediately recalled the lines, "Warhorses and chariots in the arena of fame and gain, who remembers the old setting sun in the gardens? The Han family still has bronze men's tears, flowing towards the wind, weeping for Emperor Wu." I couldn't help but feel a mix of awe and sorrow.

Dongpo's poem from prison: "Dreams linger around the clouds and mountains, my heart like a deer, my soul flies through boiling water and fire, my life like..." After being released from prison, he wrote a poem: "Facing the wine cup, I suspect it's a dream, picking up the pen, I'm already like a god." Without the slightest intention of repentance, it can be said to be unique.

75% of the world’s total; tobacco accounts for 38%; wheat for 17%; and cotton for more than half. In this way, its agricultural development not only makes full use of its geographical advantages, but also fully promotes and assists industrial production.

In the midst of such a magnificent advancement in the American economy, according to statistics from 1927, its wealth was more than 30 trillion francs, accounting for about 40% of the world’s total wealth. The total amount of cash it held in various banks at that time accounted for a large proportion of all cash in the world. As a result, the United States has become a usurious creditor to countries around the world. It not only has the qualification of being the first in the world's exports, but it is also the primary monopoly "super-profit" maker in terms of foreign investment of financial capital.

Compared to the capitalism of countries such as England and France, the economic development of the United States can be said to have grown in a short period of time. The reasons for this rapid development and enrichment should of course be scientifically explained from the particularity of American social history and geographical conditions.

The first characteristic in the history of American economic development is the absence of feudal barriers to capitalism. We know that when Europeans migrated to the United States, except for the southern regions where land was successfully divided by a feudal-like method, the northern regions were ... [text missing]. Because the southern regions formerly had a slave system, Europeans easily transplanted the feudal system there, and the natives readily accepted it. However, the northern United States had a vast area of free land. This free land had a decisive significance for the subsequent development of American capitalism.

Europeans initially only immigrated to the Atlantic coast of the northern United States. (This is the most densely populated area today.) The westward expansion from this region began in the 1770s. At that time, the central government and the state governments stipulated extremely low prices for selling land to the people. For almost a century, people could acquire land without having to pay a large price. This was the government's policy of encouraging people to move west rapidly. In 1860, the area west of the Mississippi River accounted for only one-seventh of the total population. But in 1910, the population there accounted for one-third of the country. During the latter half of the 19th century, American agriculture (except in the South) did not suffer from a lack of leased land. This situation helped farmers to develop fully and also accelerated the accumulation of capital. At that time, farmers were free owners of the land and also entrepreneurs. Because landowners can make full use of the resources on the ground, they can supply cheap raw materials to industry, and laborers in industrial centers can obtain cheap food. In particular, the result of the development of capital accumulation in agriculture itself can make the booming industrial products sell well in the domestic market. Therefore, American capitalism was characterized by the free and parallel development of agriculture and industry from the beginning. The simple reason why manpower and natural power can be coordinated in the development of industry is that American social history did not have feudal barriers to its capitalist development.

There is also another thing that we cannot ignore: that is, during the upward period of American capitalist development, it was not monopolized by larger capitalist countries of imperialism. On the contrary, the already developed British and French capitalism in Europe served as an excellent reference for the American economy. This is meaningful for both the management and technology of American capitalism.

As for studying from the characteristics of productivity, the wages paid by American capitalists were slightly higher than those in Europe. Because it was easy for laborers to acquire land and make a living, capitalists naturally had to offer higher wages to get hired when they went to work as wage laborers. Because of this, American capitalists had to find ways to increase their production efficiency in the adoption of machinery and the productivity of workers. This can be said to be the reason why American capitalists had to pay close attention to the improvement of production technology. No wonder many large capitalists or entrepreneurs spent enormous sums to organize scientific research institutes or laboratories, promoting various new inventions by many technicians and laborers. Regarding this aspect, it is of great significance in the development of the American economy.

In addition, the mechanization of American agriculture and the development of land and sea transportation have also directly affected the promotion of the manufacturing of means of production. This kind of progress in the means of production has almost completely divided and ordered the American economic system. This is also a major condition for American economic development.

As described above, the American economy has been developing smoothly. Therefore, in the nearly ten years of smooth sailing, there was little waste due to domestic riots or wars. For example, in terms of the number of troops, the current US Army has only about 110,000 people, which is less than one-third of the number of troops in Sichuan Province in China. This is a natural result of the fact that the American democratic political order is sufficient to maintain its economic system. This political and military characteristic has had great significance for the development of the American economy in the past few decades. However, since the recent crisis of American economic panic has become widespread at home and abroad, the cost of maintaining riots, strikes, and preparing for international wars has indeed exceeded that of all countries in the world.

Strong Hands 255

— Five

From the time I was born to the present, my "two hands" have spent twenty-seven years. Because of the poverty of my family's finances, from elementary school to middle school to university, I have been using and honing my "two hands," and carefully maintaining their strength - especially after stepping out of the gates of the university, I cannot but seek a way out of life through my "two hands."

—Writing brush—fountain pen—steel pen—finger pen (Note)—these are the tools that my two hands have used and utilized. —Clerk—document clerk—copyist—assistant editor—these are all the past resumes of my "two hands." But now, it has lost its "place to use its skills" after all. It is willing to sell itself to people at the lowest price - would anyone like to buy these two hands?

Sunday Literary Society

The Expression Method in Literature 260

— Innocence

The reason literature is called an "indirect art" lies in the fact that its means of expression—words—merely represent a certain concept in a conventional way. Readers accept the image's reflection and evoke the inherent concept in their minds. Only after these two concepts are mixed can they touch the true realm indicated by the literary work. At the same time, the inspiration we gain from stimuli is fleeting. To reproduce the whole picture of the spiritual feeling that exists and vanishes in an instant with dull words, even with skillful techniques, only captures a fraction of it. Therefore, the method of expression in literature is one of the important preparations for a writer—especially someone newly entering the field of literature.

We do not deny that Chinese literature has embarked on a new path in recent years, both in terms of subject matter and style. However, apart from deliberately using words to decorate dry bones and confuse the reader's vision, most of the works with life reveal a weakness in expressiveness. Because of the essay-like narration of stories, the necessary resonance is reduced, which is a major loss for the author.

Flaubert once said: "No matter what we want to express, there is only one noun; to describe its movement, there is only one verb; to assign its quality, there is only one adjective. We should patiently excavate until we seize the only noun, verb, and adjective. If we merely find something similar to these nouns, verbs, and adjectives, we must not be satisfied, and especially must not be afraid of the hardship of searching and carelessly shirk our responsibility." Flaubert's famous saying as the "single word theory" in the history of literary criticism; we believe that creators should still practice it when engaging in creative activities today. Because when depicting typical characters based on realism, the depth and extent of the character's personality depend entirely on the communication of the expression method, especially the two contradictory personalities of the intellectuals who have fallen from the petty bourgeoisie of the metropolis in the current stage. If there is an uneven exaggeration in the writing, it will become something neither donkey nor horse. In works, writers should also pay attention to the emotional part. Just as music has its high and low notes, and painting has light and dark, literature, depending on its content, should also have a crisp or melancholic tone.

The great realist Dostoevsky's distinctive feature in his works is chaotic mechanics. His descriptions of the conversations of people living in the basements of cities are rapid, fragmented sentences, with words closely repeating each other, and morbidity and dark clouds envelop the lower layers of the city. He wrote of streetlights "scattering gloom like candles in a funeral," of clocks "emitting sharp sounds like clenched throats," of small houses "like pigsties and chests," and of wind "buzzing and screaming like flies begging for food on garbage." How appropriately this tone captures the other side of the civilized metropolis! To associatively and symbolically promote the seriousness and impetus of the theme, it is necessary to have a unique vocabulary to record the tone of the metropolis's noise. This is worth learning from Dostoevsky's works. Gorky said it well: "The most important technique of literature is the study of language (i.e., words). Language is the basic material of works, especially in the novel genre. It (the novel) is a 'beautiful language' written in French or Russian. 'Beauty' is—sound, color, speech, and story, the product of human emotions and intellect created through the hands of the writer. That is, a writer uses artistic skills to harmonize content and form, and arouses people's empathy with amazing exaggeration. We call this 'beauty.'" He also said: "The true beauty of mechanical language is the correctness and clarity of the language for mood, character, and the ideas that form the work, and the influence created by this. The writer—'artist'—should have the ability to select correct, clear, and powerful language from the rich treasury of vocabulary and broad knowledge. That is, between chapters and sentences, use correct language—in the meaning represented by the language—to arrange, harmonize, and patch together, to visualize the author's thoughts and clarify the situation, so that readers can discover the vivid posture of human beings under the author's flexible brush... And—the world develops from the dynamics of struggle. Literary artists should have a careful study of language, that is, they must have the talent to choose concise, refined, appropriate, vivid, and beautiful language in order to achieve a high degree of effect in their works..."

Supplement to the Local News of Shen Bao: Film Special

An Overview of Elstree, the "Hollywood" of England 261

— Su Yin

Hollywood—this name seems too familiar to us. Needless to say, it has been recognized as the de facto "film capital" of the world for more than twenty years. But now the British film industry is not willing to lag behind and has established its own "film capital" to compete with Hollywood. This British film location is Elstree.

Hollywood—also translated as Holliwood—is because when that place was still covered with undergrowth, it was full of a kind of small tree. Its botanical name is "birds don't roost," because its branches and leaves are thorny, and birds cannot perch there. This kind of small tree is called Holly in English, so that place is called "the forest where birds don't roost." Elstree—this is still the first translation—I don't know what the original meaning is. Probably, judging from the "tree" in the name, it used to be a place where trees grew.

Elstree is a place in the suburbs of London, but like Hollywood, it has a sense of borrowing and attaching meaning. We are used to saying Hollywood—Hollywood is the entirety of the American film industry, a collective noun for the film industry. But the largest American company, MGM, is not in Hollywood, but in Culver City, which is adjacent to Hollywood. Elstree is similar. In general parlance, although it is the gathering place of the three major groups of British film companies, large British companies such as Gaumont British are in the nearby "Shepherd's Bush."

Having explained the above point, we don't need to mention it again, and just continue to treat Elstree as a synonym for the British film industry, just as we habitually use the three words Hollywood to represent the entire American film industry. However, Elstree and Hollywood have one fundamental difference. Hollywood is a colony of film industry employees, where all people related to film production, producers, directors, actors, extras, technicians, tea boys, messengers, etc., live, breathe, and work. But Elstree is just a factory. They go to work during the day, and at night they disperse and return to various parts of London, mixing in ordinary society, watching plays, dancing, or staying quietly at home. Some people say that because of this difference, Elstree will never be as full of scandalous news as Hollywood.

Elstree is five thousand five hundred miles away from Hollywood. But the terminology, symbols, gestures, etc. used in Hollywood can also be seen and heard in Elstree studios. What about silence, what about lights, what about cuts, the two places are equally noisy. In Elstree, you can see the same set bones, piled up like mountains: Shanghai's gambling den "Attention"; Dickens-era military quarters; a corner of Paris; you can see them everywhere. Therefore, except for the London smog, which is unique to Elstree, there is not much difference.

Therefore. If Hollywood actors run to Elstree and give them the same rich salary, they will definitely feel like they are at home. In the past, during the heyday of Hollywood for more than twenty years, British and European movie stars, anyone who wanted to earn a big salary and gain a great reputation, must first be baptized by Hollywood. Nearly half of the European superstars were absorbed by Hollywood. But now, Hollywood has not only released foreign stars, letting them automatically run to London, but also many American stars want to go to Elstree to make movies.

Of course, the Americans have to say grandiosely: "In the past, we borrowed half of their stars, and now we also lent many stars to them. The United Kingdom and the United States are originally brotherly countries of the same race and language. With the mutual exchange of so many stars, the friendship between the two countries will definitely become closer because of artistic mutual assistance and promotion." It must be known that the above words are diplomatic terms. The comings and goings of stars are not like university professors or lectureships, which can be exchanged through relations between the two countries. Money, money, money is the driving force behind their circulation. The UK and the US are not promoting each other, but competing with each other, trying to manipulate the hegemony of this big business, and wanting to win the world's film market.

Whoever can gather a lot of money can attract big stars, as well as technical talents, directors, writers, etc. In this war of commodity art, we return to our country, how can we reach even one ten-thousandth of others. We are the chopping board and axe, and they are the fish and meat, how can it not make people feel discouraged?

Film Review

Review of "Difficult Struggle" 262

— Zhao Ren

—Carlton—

Although generally speaking, Chinese films are progressing, individual works still show a great deal of backwardness. As recent as "Difficult Struggle" is a failed product.

Technically speaking, the stories here are not connected. The explanation of the story can satisfy the audience to a certain extent, but "Difficult Struggle" does not even achieve a direct narrative of the story. The most obvious explanation in the brochure says "On graduation day, Mr. Zhu... gave a speech to the students... Do not 'recognize' the four northeastern provinces as lost territory..." etc., but it is not on the screen, so that what Yang Guoguang said at the beginning about Mr. Zhu makes the audience confused. (As for the issue of the four northeastern provinces, even if they are not "recognized," they are still "lost territory." The issue is how to resort to a national war to recover the lost territory.) When university teachers talk about "rights" and "obligations" in jurisprudence, the clumsiness of such shots, talking for two or three minutes, also shows that the story only focuses on stiff preaching, completely losing the artistic value of the film. Lack of obvious connection, roughness, and disorganization are the biggest problems with the script. As for further discussion of the content, it cannot be said in a few words.

Not exaggerating at all, the directing or acting here shows vulgarity and naivety. The author of "Like Water Flowing Years" has regressed to such an extent. Here, there is only clumsy preaching, not the expression of film art. As for business, it will also give producers a good practical lesson.

Random Notes on "The Man Who Reclaimed His Head" 263

— Guo Cheng

"The Man Who Reclaimed His Head" is another anti-war film with serious contemporary significance.

The burden of war, the sins of war, the hypocrisy and deception of war, the terror of war, and the crimes of those who do evil through war are all nakedly exposed in "The Man Who Reclaimed His Head."

The performance of such a film for us on the eve of the secret deployment of the clouds of World War II cannot be said to be meaningless.

Among the actors, Claude Rains plays the lead role in this film. He previously starred in "Invisible Man" and "Crime Without Passion" and became famous. Joan Bennett plays the female lead in this film. Her past successful works include "Bulldog Drammond" and other films. In addition, in this film, the three-year-old child star Baby Jane has a very sensational performance. She has previously appeared in "Have A Heart" and "Were Rich Again"; she has recently played a very important role in the world-shocking great ethical film "Imitation of Lmitation of Lito" (Chinese name "Spring Breeze Autumn Rain". This film will also come to China).

Tianyi Company's new sound film "Difficult Struggle" premiered at Carlton today

The New Lineup of the Diantong Company 264

The Diantong Company, which owns its own newly invented "Three Friends Sound Recorder," made its debut with "The Ordeal of Peach and Plum," which was made with new talents and new technologies. After the amazing success, it actively expanded internally and strived to enrich itself. Based on scientific, collective, and efficient production methods and talent-based principles; in this thriving audience, before the New Year of 1935, the factory site problem was first solved. The new site on Jingzhou Road now has a wide field and a beautiful environment. The park is equipped with quietness and complete sports equipment, so not only is work efficiency great, but it is also very suitable for everyone's physical and mental health and artistic recuperation. In the "dark film circle" viewed by society, Diantong is moving towards a bright and brilliant artistic future. Recently, in addition to successfully completing the second sound film, "Sons and Daughters in a Time of Upheaval," directed by the new director Xu Xingzhi, and starring the new photographer Wu Yinxian and Yuan Muzhi and Wang Renmei, the third new film will be launched, which will be directed by the new director Situ Huimin and the famous photographer Yang Xiaoming. A group of new artists are heading to the screen in an active and tense mood, based on the spirit of artistic creation, and will definitely shine with a unique brilliance in art.

"A Grand View of Chinese Movie Stars" 265

The Yisheng Publishing House at 133 Yuanmingyuan Road in this city has attracted the attention of ordinary fans since it published "A Grand View of Chinese Movie Stars." Its rich content, editing skills, and superb printing can be called the first great picture book in Chinese film history. It is reported that it has entrusted the Shanghai Magazine Company on Simalu to make reservations, from March 15 to the end of March. An extension of ten days is allowed for other cities. It is scheduled to be published on April 10.

Various News from Lianhua 266

Lianhua is actively preparing to produce sound films and will centralize its factories. The original factory site of the First Factory in Xujiahui, Shanghai, has been expanded to more than three times its size, becoming the largest studio in the Chinese film industry. The surrounding real estate is inhabited by Lianhua staff and actors. Operating a large-scale film village.

"Vicious Beauty," written and directed by Yang Xiaozhong, starring Chen Yanyan and Zhang Zhi, and with a guest appearance by Liang Saizhen, has been playing at the Jincheng Grand Theater in Shanghai since the 6th of this month. The plot of this film is moving, and the performance is powerful, and the audience is satisfied. Therefore, since its release, the audience has been very enthusiastic.

"National Style," co-directed by Luo Mingyou and Zhu Shilin, is only one street scene away from completion. The completed film was previewed a few days ago, and the results were excellent.

All of "Carefree Gentleman" has been filmed. It can be released at the end of this month. Because this film is the most effortful work in the national comedy film, it is entirely dubbed by Lianhua's new sound machine, so it has attracted much attention from the society. The release of this film will be a sensation.

Lianhua Pictorial has been welcomed by general readers since its renovation and expansion. In order to strive for excellence, the magazine will change the cover to a two-color printing from Volume 5, Issue 7.

Lei Ying Novel

The Hate of India's National Subjugation (Clive of India) (1) 267

— Mao De

Produced by the 20th Century Company of America, starring Ronald Colman and Loretta Young

Robert Clive was a madman—at least that's what many clerks of the British East India Trading Company believed at the time. Clive was stubborn by nature. He hated the extravagance of ordinary merchants. He hated the mechanical life of clerks, registering endless numbers in large ledgers every day. He disobeyed his superiors' orders. As a clerk, he hired someone to hold an umbrella for him. In the Indian daytime, the scorching sun was unbearable, but as a clerk, he shouldn't be afraid of the heat. Clive's ignorance of his own limits greatly angered Pemberton. What made people think he was crazy was that he openly accused Johnston's door plate of being fraudulent. Johnston also worked for the same company, but his position was higher than his. Johnston wanted to duel with him. Clive agreed. But when the two heroes met, Clive only fired a blank shot into the air. Johnston watched the young man's arrogance and couldn't help but feel angry, but he couldn't raise his gun.

But he was unwilling to show weakness and deliberately threatened: "Do you still dare to say I'm cheating?" Clive replied: "I still say you're cheating! You have the ability to shoot!" Johnston still couldn't raise his gun. After a while, he threw the gun on the ground with a ashamed face and walked away, muttering hatefully: "This man is crazy!" This man is crazy, everyone believed again this time, except for Edmond Macsgreen. Macsgreen's feelings for Clive were always the same, and he was deeply convinced.

In the mid-18th century, the wealth of India's treasures and products was beyond the wildest dreams of imperialists. Gold and silver everywhere, rare spices, and priceless treasures made desperate young people from the Netherlands, Portugal, England, France, and other countries willing to travel across the ocean and endure all kinds of hardships to come to the tropical region where it was hot all year round and there were widespread miasma. All they wanted was to plunder some treasures and money, load them up and return home, and never have to worry about eating and wearing them for the rest of their lives. However, since the races and nationalities were so diverse, they began to hate and kill each other. Everyone hid behind someone else, wanting to get a chance to grab his throat, kill him, and seize more treasures. They especially liked to collude with the local tribes, borrowing a knife to kill people and drive out people of another nationality, so that they could enjoy trade! Simplicity is the monopoly of looting. So the white people in India, because of different nationalities, began to kill each other freely.

Day after day, long caravans of camels carried all kinds of treasures to the trading pier. Day after day, merchant ships loaded with treasures crossed the ocean and transported them to Europe. This outflow of financial resources has continued for many years without exhaustion. The officials stationed in various countries, the big merchants, have successively packed up and returned to their hometowns and became rich men. However, the clerks in the company, with their humble status, seemed to never have a share of unexpected wealth except for a limited salary. But despite having no share, who didn't come with extravagant hopes? Robert Clive was one of them.

Clive came to India and lived a tasteless bookkeeping life, and felt restless. He said angrily to Macsgreen: "If I had known that this kind of life was all empty, I would have committed suicide!" Edmond comforted him: "Calm down. Don't make a fuss. If you keep making a fuss, we will have no place to stay." Clive frowned and pondered. He suddenly saw his friend's neck with a thin gold chain hanging, with a small gold box hanging below. He had seen it before. But this time, he unconsciously held the thing in his hand. (To be continued)
